# Audit Log

Append-only record of completed-step audits. Each audited step gets one entry per auditing agent.

The Ralph-loop audit prompt and audit-only launchers use this file to decide which completed steps remain eligible for each agent. An entry by `Codex` makes that step ineligible for future Codex audits, but it does not make the step ineligible for `Claude Code`. An entry by `Claude Code` works the same way in the opposite direction.

Required entry shape:

```md
## <UTC timestamp> - <step_id> <step_title> - <agent>

- status: completed|blocked
- agent: Codex|Claude Code
- model: <model>
- effort: <effort>
- step_id: <step_id>
- step_title: <step_title>
- prior_audits: <agent/status/finding summary or none>
- correctness_findings: <summary or none>
- performance_findings: <summary or none>
- improvement_findings: <summary or none>
- corrective_action: <summary or none>
- files_changed: <semicolon-separated paths or none>
- tests_run: <semicolon-separated commands or none>
- follow_up: <summary or none>
```

## 2026-04-25T19:40:16Z - 03-013 implement-fatal-error-handling - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 03-013
- step_title: implement-fatal-error-handling
- prior_audits: none (no prior AUDIT_LOG entry; HANDOFF_LOG records Codex completion of the original implementation only)
- correctness_findings: extractFatalErrorMessage in src/playable/bun-runtime-entry-point/implementFatalErrorHandling.ts called fatalError.message.trim() unconditionally inside the `instanceof Error` branch. Empirically reproduced — `Object.create(Error.prototype)` and a real `new Error()` whose `.message` was redefined to `undefined` both pass `instanceof Error` while `typeof .message === 'undefined'`, and `.trim()` then threw `TypeError: undefined is not an object (evaluating 'fatalError.message.trim')`. That defect lived inside the *fatal error handler itself*, where a thrown error has nowhere to be caught (the launcher's outer `void main().catch` would already be servicing the original fatal). Implementation otherwise satisfies Expected Changes: contract object is `as const`, runtime command guard rejects non-`bun run doom.ts` callers with the literal expected message, deterministic-replay flags are all false at phase `pre-session-launch`, and the focused test still pins the contract SHA-256 (3148335646ca0fc8e21171fb4e4ee389716b96265748769f7c94aac5b1f745da, recomputed live via Bun.CryptoHasher) and cross-checks the 01-007 audit manifest, package.json `start` script, and `src/main.ts` HELP_TEXT plus catch/stderr/exit fatal path.
- performance_findings: none — fatal handler runs at most once per process exit; no hot-path allocations or per-frame work involved.
- improvement_findings: focused test exercised only `Error` with valid message, `Error` with whitespace-only message, and the non-Bun command rejection path. The plain-`string` branch of extractFatalErrorMessage and the unknown-fallback path for null, undefined, plain objects, arrays, numbers, booleans, and Errors with non-string messages were not directly tested, masking the undefined-message crash and leaving four other branches drift-unprotected.
- corrective_action: Hardened extractFatalErrorMessage with a `typeof fatalError.message === 'string'` guard so a non-string `.message` falls through to the next branch instead of throwing. Contract object value (and therefore its pinned SHA-256) is unchanged. Added three regression tests covering the trimmed plain-string path, a parameterized fallback sweep across `''`, `'   '`, `null`, `undefined`, `0`, `42`, `true`, `false`, `{}`, `[]`, and two Errors whose `.message` was redefined to `undefined`/`42`, and a result-identity test asserting the result reuses the contract's auditedCurrentLauncherSurface and deterministicReplayCompatibility references and pins the literal status/exitCode/outputStream/runtimeCommand fields. Test count grew from 6 (17 expects) to 9 (36 expects).
- files_changed: src/playable/bun-runtime-entry-point/implementFatalErrorHandling.ts; test/playable/bun-runtime-entry-point/implement-fatal-error-handling.test.ts; plan_fps/AUDIT_LOG.md
- tests_run: bun test test/playable/bun-runtime-entry-point/implement-fatal-error-handling.test.ts; bun test; bun x tsc --noEmit --project tsconfig.json

Function correctly handles all five state transitions: wrong runtime → throws; phase ≠ tryRunTics → 'skip' with paused: !isFocused and resetApplied: false; tryRunTics + !isFocused → 'pause' with resetApplied: false; tryRunTics + !wasFocused + isFocused → 'resume' with reset called and resetApplied: true; tryRunTics + wasFocused + isFocused → 'continue'. Test count grew from 6 (12 expects) to 9 (20 expects). No production code change required.

## 2026-04-25T20:10:48Z - 09-009 apply-palette-effects-and-gamma - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 09-009
- step_title: apply-palette-effects-and-gamma
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: applyPaletteEffectsAndGamma in src/playable/rendering-product-integration/applyPaletteEffectsAndGamma.ts satisfies Expected Changes — PALETTE_EFFECTS_AND_GAMMA_COMMAND_CONTRACT pins entryFile 'doom.ts' / runtimeCommand 'bun run doom.ts', the function rejects non-Bun-runtime callers, validates byteLength on framebuffer (64000), gammaTable (256), palette (768), and presentationFramebuffer (256000), validates paletteEffect.{red,green,blue} integer 0..255 and paletteEffect.strength integer 0..256, and writes RGBA bytes via the rounded-blend formula `((source*(0x100-strength) + target*strength + 0x80) >> 8) & 0xff` then `gammaTable[blended]` over a full 320x200 frame. Boundary inputs strength=0 collapses to gammaTable[palette[i]] (palette+gamma pass-through) and strength=256 collapses to gammaTable[targetColor] (full target replacement); all 64000 pixels and the FNV-1a-style framebuffer/presentation checksums verified byte-identical against the prior implementation after the performance refactor. The test file's pinned EXPECTED_PRESENTATION_SHA256, EXPECTED_FRAMEBUFFER_CHECKSUM, EXPECTED_PRESENTATION_CHECKSUM, and EXPECTED_FIRST/LAST_PRESENTATION_BYTES all still match the new implementation, proving algorithm output is unchanged.
- performance_findings: Hot loop ran 64000 iterations and accessed `context.{framebuffer,gammaTable,palette,presentationFramebuffer}` (~10x per iter) and `context.paletteEffect.{red,green,blue,strength}` (~12x per iter via the inner `blendChannel` call) — roughly 23 property reads per pixel × 64000 = 1,472,000 property reads per frame. Additionally `context.paletteEffect.red/green/blue` were re-multiplied by `strength` 192,000 times per frame (3 channels × 64000) when the products are loop-invariant, and `pixelIndex * PRESENTATION_BYTES_PER_PIXEL` recomputed offsets each iteration when an accumulated `presentationOffset += 4` would suffice. The non-inlined `blendChannel(source, target, strength, inverseStrength)` helper added 192,000 function-call frames per frame.
- improvement_findings: 9 missing-coverage paths in test/playable/rendering-product-integration/apply-palette-effects-and-gamma.test.ts — invalid framebuffer/gammaTable/palette/presentationFramebuffer byteLengths (each both above and below the expected size, plus the zero-byte case), invalid paletteEffect.{red,green,blue} below 0 / above 0xff / non-integer (and Infinity), strength below 0 / above 0x100 / non-integer / NaN, the strength=0 boundary (palette+gamma pass-through), and the strength=256 boundary (full target color replacement). Test 4 only covered strength=0x101. Result.paletteEffect referential identity (`result.paletteEffect === input.paletteEffect`) was also unprotected.
- corrective_action: Refactored applyPaletteEffectsAndGamma to (1) hoist context.framebuffer/gammaTable/palette/presentationFramebuffer/paletteEffect to locals, (2) hoist paletteEffect.strength + the loop-invariant target*strength products into pre-multiplied locals (targetRedScaled/targetGreenScaled/targetBlueScaled), (3) inline the blendChannel formula into the hot loop body, (4) replace `pixelIndex * PRESENTATION_BYTES_PER_PIXEL` with an accumulating `presentationOffset += PRESENTATION_BYTES_PER_PIXEL`, and (5) delete the now-unused blendChannel helper. The blend formula and FNV-1a checksum sequence are byte-identical to the prior implementation. Updated the test's EXPECTED_SOURCE_SHA256 to `99241bad3b9e0ba8472d0765a079b576b18aae6021fb316ad8622fa72fcf00f9` (recomputed via Bun.CryptoHasher) and added 22 new regression assertions: a parameterized 9-case byte-length rejection (each branch of assertByteLength × negative/zero/over case), a parameterized 14-case paletteEffect rejection covering blue/green/red bounds plus integer/NaN/Infinity guards and strength bounds plus non-integer/NaN guards, a strength=0 boundary test (full-frame SHA-256 hash compare against an oracle-computed expected buffer plus an independent gammaTable[palette[paletteIndex*3+offset]] sampled-pixel check at index 12345), a strength=256 boundary test (full-frame SHA-256 hash compare against a constant-color expected buffer with explicit gamma-table value pins 0xdf/0xbf/0x7f), and a `result.paletteEffect === fixture.paletteEffect` identity assertion in the existing golden test. Test count grew from 4 (22 expects) to 28 (78 expects).
- files_changed: src/playable/rendering-product-integration/applyPaletteEffectsAndGamma.ts; test/playable/rendering-product-integration/apply-palette-effects-and-gamma.test.ts; plan_fps/AUDIT_LOG.md

- improvement_findings: (1) Test did not include any `Object.isFrozen` assertions on INJECT_DEMO_SCRIPTED_INPUT_CONTRACT or its scriptedEventTypes/supportedDoomKeys frozen fields, nor on the result object or its heldKeys/injectedEvents arrays — a regression dropping any Object.freeze in the contract or the function would not be caught; (2) test used WebCrypto `crypto.subtle.digest('SHA-256', ...)` plus a manual byte→hex padStart loop where the convention codified by the 01-007/02-015/03-005/03-013/06-014/09-009/05-005/01-005 audit fix-passes is `new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(...).digest('hex')`; (3) test used `parseAuditManifest` + `JSON.parse(await Bun.file(path).text())` where the convention is the one-call `Bun.file(path).json()`; (4) 12 missing-coverage paths — empty scriptedEvents (returns empty injectedEvents and unchanged nextScriptIndex), nextScriptIndex === scriptedEvents.length (cursor at end), future-tic-only events (early break with no throw and no consumption), same-tic source-order preservation (3 events at the same tic preserve insertion order in injectedEvents), heldKeys output sortedness, parameterized currentTic rejection (negative, non-integer, NaN), parameterized nextScriptIndex rejection (negative, non-integer, over-bounds), scriptedEvent.tic rejection (negative integer, non-integer), unsupported event type rejection (non-keydown/keyup), and unsupported held key rejection.
- corrective_action: Replaced WebCrypto-based sha256Hex with `new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(value).digest('hex')` (synchronous, no TextEncoder allocation) — same SHA-256 digest, so the pinned EXPECTED_CONTRACT_HASH ('1cfafbebd26737413b6d070051087ac70ee155354ad12b7e3124dd43002d15d4') is unchanged. Boundary checks: empty input returns frozen empty array with TICCMD_SIZE/EMPTY_TICCMD identity; mid-list unsupported event throws on the unsupported entry without leaking the result; mid-list unmapped scan code (0x59 in the existing test) is dropped while preserving inputIndex of subsequent kept entries. - performance_findings: The hot loop iterated `inputEvents.entries()`, which allocates a fresh array iterator and yields a 2-element [number, T] tuple per iteration. While Win32 keyboard message volume is bounded (well under 35Hz), the entries() allocation is unnecessary — the function only needs the index and the indexed element, both available via direct indexing. Additionally, inputEvent.lparam was read three times per accepted entry (translateScanCode, isExtendedKey, extractScanCode) when one local read would suffice.

The inputIndex semantics, drop-unmapped semantics, and result shape are byte-identical. Added Object.isFrozen on result and result.orderedEvents in both happy-path tests, and added a per-element `for (const orderedEvent of result.orderedEvents) expect(Object.isFrozen(orderedEvent)).toBe(true)` loop. Added `expect(result.ticCommandTemplate).toBe(EMPTY_TICCMD)` referential-identity assertion to the primary happy-path test. Added a new 'returns a frozen empty result for an empty event list' regression test that asserts an empty result.orderedEvents, frozen result/orderedEvents, ticCommandSize===TICCMD_SIZE, and ticCommandTemplate===EMPTY_TICCMD. Function rejects non-Bun runtime, validates indexedFramebuffer.length===64000 and playpalPalette.length===768, builds a 256-entry Uint32Array palette lookup via blue | (green << 8) | (red << 16) | 0xff000000 over each 3-byte BGR (read in RGB-source-order then composed) entry, and runs a 64000-pixel hot loop writing presentedFramebuffer[i] = paletteLookup[indexedFramebuffer[i]]. Result is Object.freeze({contract, paletteLookup, presentedFramebuffer}). Boundary verified: an all-zero indexedFramebuffer produces a uniform paletteLookup[0] frame across all 64000 entries; a 0/256/missing-byte palette is rejected with 'Expected PLAYPAL byte length 768'; a 0/64000±1-byte framebuffer is rejected with 'Expected indexed framebuffer byte length 64000'. The contract.indexedFramebufferWidth/Height match windowPolicy.ts SCREENWIDTH=320/SCREENHEIGHT=200. Pre-audit test (4 cases, 25 expects) covered the contract value+hash, the manifest+source cross-check, a 4-pixel deterministic happy path (indices 0/1/2/63999), and a wrong-runtime rejection — but did not cover Object.isFrozen on the contract, indexed-framebuffer or palette length-mismatch rejection paths (over and under), the all-zero indexed-buffer baseline, or a full-frame golden hash.
- performance_findings: Hot loop ran 64000 iterations and accessed `options.indexedFramebuffer.length` in the loop guard plus `options.indexedFramebuffer[pixelIndex]` per iteration — two redirected property reads through `options` per iteration that are loop-invariant after the boundary validation. `buildPaletteLookup` similarly re-read `APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT.paletteEntries` (loop guard, 256 reads), `APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT.paletteEntryBytes` (256 reads inside the loop), `APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT.greenShift/redShift/alphaMask` (256 reads each — three contract property accesses per palette entry × 256 entries = 768 redundant property reads per frame). Pre-multiplication wasn't applicable here (the BGR composition is per-entry pixel data), but hoisting the contract constants to locals removes the property indirection.
- improvement_findings: (1) Test used `node:crypto.createHash` for the contract hash where the convention codified across the 01-007/02-015/03-005/03-013/06-014/09-009/05-005/01-005/00-011/00-012/06-012/06-005/02-005/02-016/08-004 audit fix-passes is `new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(...).digest('hex')`; (2) test used `JSON.parse(await Bun.file(path).text())` plus a multi-step `Reflect.get(...) + typeof === 'object' + Reflect.get(...)` access chain where the convention is the one-call `Bun.file(path).json()` with a typed JSON shape; (3) no Object.isFrozen assertions on APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT or on the result wrapper; (4) no rejection-path coverage for indexed framebuffers of length 0, 63999, or 64001; (5) no rejection-path coverage for PLAYPAL palettes of length 0, 767, or 769; (6) no all-zero-indexed-buffer baseline that locks `presentedFramebuffer[i] === paletteLookup[0]` across all 64000 pixels; (7) no full-frame SHA-256 golden across the entire 256000-byte presentedFramebuffer that would catch a regression in any single one of the 64000 indexed lookups (the prior 4-pixel sample spot-checks indices 0/1/2/63999 only); (8) windowPolicy SCREEN constants were asserted via hard-coded literal strings 'export const SCREENHEIGHT = 200;' / 'export const SCREENWIDTH = 320;' that would silently desync if either contract field changed but the literal was not updated — should derive the substring from the contract's indexedFramebufferHeight/Width fields.
- corrective_action: Replaced `node:crypto.createHash` with `new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(JSON.stringify(...)).digest('hex')` and removed the unused node:crypto import. Replaced `JSON.parse(await Bun.file(AUDIT_MANIFEST_PATH).text())` plus the Reflect.get access chain with `(await Bun.file(AUDIT_MANIFEST_PATH).json()) as PlayableHostSurfaceManifest` using a local `interface PlayableHostSurfaceManifest { readonly currentLauncherHostTransition: { readonly call: string } }` typed shape. Refactored applyPlaypalPalette to (a) hoist `options.indexedFramebuffer` and `options.indexedFramebuffer.length` to locals (`indexedFramebuffer`, `indexedFramebufferLength`) so the hot loop guard and lookup avoid the `options.` property indirection; (b) hoist `paletteEntries`, `paletteEntryBytes`, `greenShift`, `redShift`, `alphaMask` from APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT to locals at the top of `buildPaletteLookup` so the per-entry palette composition reads from locals instead of frozen-object properties. Reordered the BGR byte reads inside `buildPaletteLookup` to red→green→blue source order (matching the byte order in PLAYPAL) so the read sequence reads the source bytes in ascending offset. The output palette word value is unchanged because the OR composition is commutative. Verified the contract SHA-256 hash (3bdb2278339f4d335fb0ab8683ba611d116ff16ec5078f361d671f76831d81d0) is unchanged via Bun.CryptoHasher of JSON.stringify(APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT). Added Object.isFrozen assertions on the contract (test 1) and on the result wrapper (test 3). Replaced the hard-coded SCREEN literal strings with `\`export const SCREENHEIGHT = ${APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT.indexedFramebufferHeight};\`` / `\`export const SCREENWIDTH = ${APPLY_PLAYPAL_PALETTE_CONTRACT.indexedFramebufferWidth};\`` template literals derived from the contract — drift in either contract field now flows into the assertion. Added a full-frame SHA-256 golden over the 256000-byte presentedFramebuffer (`adbd2682d1592f57eef0825c891fe736248e83ffc003731325ac41d342b6282d`, recomputed via Bun.CryptoHasher of the live output) to test 3 so any regression in any of the 64000 palette lookups would be caught. Added a new 'maps an all-zero indexed framebuffer to a uniform paletteLookup[0] frame' regression test that uses a 0xab/0xcd/0xef PLAYPAL entry 0, asserts paletteLookup[0]===((0xff000000 | (0xab << 16) | (0xcd << 8) | 0xef) >>> 0) (the >>> 0 unsigned-cast required because JS bitwise OR on a 0x80000000+ value produces a signed-int result that doesn't compare against the Uint32Array's unsigned read), then loops over all 64000 presentedFramebuffer pixels asserting each equals the expected unsigned value. Added two parameterized test.each blocks: (a) 3 cases for indexed framebuffer length rejection (0, 63999, 64001) with full literal expected error message; (b) 3 cases for PLAYPAL byte length rejection (0, 767, 769) with full literal expected error message. Test count grew from 4 (25 expects) to 11 (31 expects via test.each parameterization).

- step_id: 09-006

- correctness_findings: renderIntermissionScreens in src/playable/rendering-product-integration/renderIntermissionScreens.ts satisfies Expected Changes — RENDER_INTERMISSION_SCREENS_COMMAND_CONTRACT pins entryFile 'doom.ts' / runtimeCommand 'bun run doom.ts' (matching the live 01-012 manifest's commandContracts.target), the function rejects non-Bun-runtime callers, validates framebuffer.length === 64000, backgroundPixels.length === 64000, screenKind ∈ {'entering','finished','stats'}, sourceName non-empty, completedMap non-empty, enteringMap non-empty when present (or null), totalTics non-negative integer, and per-layer height/width positive integer, transparentPaletteIndex 0..255 integer, and pixels.length === width*height. The hot loop in drawLayer correctly maps each layer pixel to its framebuffer position with row+column clipping against [0, SCREENHEIGHT) and [0, SCREENWIDTH), skipping transparent pixels and incrementing drawnPixelCount only for written pixels. computeFramebufferChecksum uses FNV-1a (offset basis 0x811c9dc5, prime 0x01000193) for a deterministic 32-bit checksum that locks every byte of the framebuffer post-blit. Boundary verified for off-screen (x>=SCREENWIDTH-2/y>=SCREENHEIGHT-2 → 4 in-bounds pixels; x=-2/y=-2 → 1 in-bounds bottom-right corner pixel) and fully-transparent layer (drawnPixelCount===0, framebuffer matches background). However, validateLayer omitted `Number.isInteger(layer.x)` and `Number.isInteger(layer.y)` checks — non-integer x/y would silently produce NaN-indexed framebuffer writes (TypedArray drops them) while still incrementing drawnPixelCount. Pre-audit test (5 cases, 19 expects) covered the contract, the finished-map happy path with patch layer, episode-complete transition, wrong-runtime rejection, and one layer pixel-buffer length rejection — but did not cover transparent-pixel skipping, off-screen layer clipping at any of the four edges/corners, the `entering` screenKind, and the validateOptions rejection paths for framebuffer length / background length / unknown screenKind / empty sourceName / empty completedMap / empty enteringMap when present / negative or non-integer totalTics / layer height invalid (zero, negative, non-integer, NaN) / layer width invalid / layer transparentPaletteIndex out of range or non-integer / layer x/y non-integer.
- performance_findings: (1) Contract object had `as const` for type-level immutability but no runtime `Object.freeze`, leaving the runtime shape mutable and inconsistent with the freeze convention codified across the 04-012/05-005/09-009/06-005/06-014/06-012 audit fix-passes; (2) drawLayer hot loop accessed `layer.height`, `layer.width`, `layer.x`, `layer.y`, `layer.transparentPaletteIndex`, and `layer.pixels` per iteration through frozen-object property reads instead of hoisted locals — for a typical 4×3 patch that is ~12×6=72 redundant property reads; (3) computeFramebufferChecksum iterated `for (const paletteIndex of framebuffer)` over 64000 bytes using the iterator protocol where a direct index loop avoids the per-iteration iterator-result allocation.
- improvement_findings: (1) No `Object.isFrozen` assertion on RENDER_INTERMISSION_SCREENS_COMMAND_CONTRACT — a regression dropping any future freeze would not be caught; (2) 28 missing-coverage paths — transparent-pixel skipping, bottom-right clip, top-left clip, `entering` screenKind happy path with empty layers, framebuffer length rejection (0, 63999, 64001), background length rejection (0, 63999, 64001), unknown screenKind rejection, empty sourceName / completedMap / enteringMap rejection, totalTics rejection (negative, fractional, NaN), layer height rejection (zero, negative, fractional, NaN), layer width rejection (same four), layer transparentPaletteIndex rejection (-1, 256, fractional, NaN), and the new layer x/y non-integer rejection paths.
- corrective_action: Wrapped RENDER_INTERMISSION_SCREENS_COMMAND_CONTRACT in `Object.freeze(...as const)` so the runtime shape matches the readonly type contract. Hoisted layer.height/width/x/y/pixels/transparentPaletteIndex into locals at the top of drawLayer so the hot loop reads from locals instead of frozen-object properties; also hoisted the framebuffer row offset (`framebufferRowIndex * SCREENWIDTH`) and layer row offset (`layerRowIndex * layerWidth`) once per outer-loop iteration so the inner loop computes only the column-relative offset. Replaced the iterator-protocol loop in computeFramebufferChecksum with an index-based loop reading framebuffer[byteIndex] from a hoisted byteCount local. Added `Number.isInteger(layer.x)` and `Number.isInteger(layer.y)` validation in validateLayer with the literal error messages 'Intermission layer ${layerIndex} x must be an integer.' and 'Intermission layer ${layerIndex} y must be an integer.'. Added an `Object.isFrozen(RENDER_INTERMISSION_SCREENS_COMMAND_CONTRACT) === true` assertion to the contract-locking test. Added six narrative regression tests (entering screenKind happy path, transparent-pixel skipping with full-screen identity hash, bottom-right corner clip, top-left corner clip) plus eight parameterized test.each blocks covering framebuffer length rejection (3 cases), background length rejection (3 cases), totalTics rejection (3 cases: -1, 1.5, NaN), layer height rejection (4 cases), layer width rejection (4 cases), layer transparentPaletteIndex rejection (4 cases: -1, 256, 1.5, NaN), and layer x/y non-integer rejection (4 cases). The framebuffer checksum (3,888,271,315) and SHA-256 hash ('407f74eca6f8b92bbea9c62263dbaff7798bd45c320cc4df405fb0b61904d4c0') in the existing happy-path test still match exactly after the performance refactor, confirming byte-identical output. Test count grew from 5 (19 expects) to 38 (68 expects).

- status: completed

- model: claude-opus-4-7

- step_title: add-framebuffer-hash-test-hooks
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: addFramebufferHashTestHooks in src/playable/rendering-product-integration/addFramebufferHashTestHooks.ts satisfies Expected Changes — ADD_FRAMEBUFFER_HASH_TEST_HOOKS_COMMAND='bun run doom.ts', ADD_FRAMEBUFFER_HASH_TEST_HOOKS_AUDIT_SCHEMA_VERSION=1, ADD_FRAMEBUFFER_HASH_TEST_HOOKS_MISSING_SURFACE='framebuffer-hash-capture-hook' (matching the live 01-012 manifest's framebuffer-hash-capture-hook explicit-null surface). The factory rejects any non-Bun runtimeCommand at the boundary, derives a viewport from computeViewport(screenBlocks, detailMode), and returns an Object.freeze'd hooks object {captureFramebufferHash, command, detailMode, screenBlocks}. captureFramebufferHash validates options.framebuffer.length===64000, frameNumber non-negative integer, tag non-empty, optional previousFramebuffer.length===64000, then returns evidence with changedByteCount (0 if previousFramebuffer is undefined; otherwise per-byte diff count over 64000 entries), command, frameNumber, fullFramebufferChecksum (running multiply-and-add scaled by byteIndex+1 with >>>0 wrap), fullFramebufferHash (Bun.CryptoHasher SHA-256 over the whole frame), tag, transitionHash (Bun.CryptoHasher SHA-256 over previousFramebuffer || nothing, then framebuffer — so for undefined previous it equals fullFramebufferHash and for identical previous and current it doubles the bytes), and viewport {checksum, hash, height: viewport.viewHeight, width: viewport.scaledViewWidth (pre-detailshift), x: viewport.viewWindowX, y: viewport.viewWindowY}. Pre-audit test (4 cases, 13 expects) covered the contract value, the deterministic full-frame happy path at setblocks=9/high-detail, the missing-surface manifest cross-check, the wrong-runtime rejection, and one previousFramebuffer length rejection — but did not cover the deterministic-replay-across-calls invariant, the identical previous/current framebuffer (changedByteCount=0 with doubled-buffer transitionHash) path, the undefined previousFramebuffer (changedByteCount=0 with single-buffer transitionHash equals fullFramebufferHash) path, the setblocks=11 full-screen viewport (viewWindowX=0, viewWindowY=0, viewport.hash equals fullFramebufferHash) path, the low-detail-mode viewport (DetailMode.low echoed in hooks.detailMode), the framebuffer length rejection paths (0, 63999, 64001), the frameNumber rejection paths (-1, 1.5, NaN), and the empty-tag rejection path.
- performance_findings: Hot loops over 64000 bytes (computeByteChecksum, countChangedBytes) and the viewport area (computeViewportChecksum, computeViewportHash, ~41472 bytes for setblocks=9) read `framebuffer.length` / `viewport.viewWindowY` / `viewport.viewWindowX` / `viewport.viewHeight` / `viewport.scaledViewWidth` per iteration as loop guards / row-offset terms — these are loop-invariant once computed. For computeViewportChecksum that is ~3 viewport-property reads × 144 outer × 288 inner = 124,416 redundant property reads per frame; for computeViewportHash similar but with subarray construction. Hashing hooks may be invoked once per visible tic during deterministic replay, so the per-frame property indirection compounds.
- improvement_findings: (1) No Object.isFrozen assertion on the returned hooks object — a regression dropping the Object.freeze in addFramebufferHashTestHooks would not be caught; (2) 9 missing-coverage branches identified above; (3) "rejects invalid previous framebuffers before capture evidence is produced" asserted framebuffer remained unchanged but the function does not mutate the framebuffer in any path, making the assertion vacuous (kept anyway as a defensive lock against a future regression that introduces in-place mutation).
- corrective_action: Refactored computeByteChecksum, countChangedBytes, computeViewportChecksum, and computeViewportHash to hoist `framebuffer.length` (or viewport.viewWindowY/viewWindowX/viewHeight/scaledViewWidth) into locals before the loops, and pre-computed the row-end limits (yEnd, xEnd) once per call. The hashing arithmetic (running checksum, FNV-1a-style multiply-and-add, SHA-256 sequential update over per-row subarrays) is preserved byte-identical, confirmed by the existing happy-path test still passing the pinned fullFramebufferChecksum=3,425,308,800, fullFramebufferHash='b4f0d2b9a424beb742351d4d90b3ed45470af1e0c02fb217231215a8581b387b', viewport.checksum=2,264,032,128, and viewport.hash='298920bce846c3eab8becff9aade99fc1fd089778621f70843e69bb83e1e085c' values. Added Object.isFrozen(hooks) assertion in the contract-locking test. Added five new regression tests: 'produces deterministic evidence across repeated calls with identical inputs' (locks deterministicReplay invariant), 'reports zero changed bytes and the doubled-buffer transition hash for identical previous and current framebuffers' (locks the previous=current path against an oracle-computed Bun.CryptoHasher result), 'handles undefined previousFramebuffer by reporting zero changed bytes and a single-buffer transition hash' (locks the previousFramebuffer===undefined path; transitionHash equals fullFramebufferHash since the SHA-256 inputs are identical), 'reports the full screen viewport when screenBlocks is at the maximum' (locks setblocks=11 with viewport.x=0/y=0/width=320/height=200 and viewport.hash===fullFramebufferHash), and 'preserves the unshifted scaledViewWidth in the viewport evidence under low detail mode' (locks DetailMode.low pass-through with width=288/height=144). Added three parameterized test.each blocks covering framebuffer length rejection (0, 63999, 64001), frameNumber rejection (-1, 1.5, NaN), and an empty-tag rejection test. Test count grew from 4 (13 expects) to 16 (37 expects).

The function `defineMouseCapturePolicy` validates the runtime command at the boundary (throws when not 'bun run doom.ts'), then resolves to the focus-loss policy whenever `hasWindowFocus===false` (priority over inputOwner), then to the deterministic-replay policy when `inputOwner==='deterministic-replay'`, then to the menu-active policy when `inputOwner==='menu'`, otherwise returns the captured `gameplay-focus` policy. Every released policy returns `replaySafeTicCommand=EMPTY_TICCMD`, `replaySafeTicCommandBytes=TICCMD_SIZE` (8), `shouldClipCursorToWindow=false`, `shouldHideCursor=false` — matching the deterministic-replay neutral ticcmd contract from step 06-007 and `01-010-audit-missing-live-input.json`. The captured policy returns `shouldClipCursorToWindow=true, shouldHideCursor=true` and the same neutral replay-safe ticcmd. Test 2 cross-validates the live manifest at `plan_fps/manifests/01-010-audit-missing-live-input.json` via a typed predicate (`isMissingLiveInputManifest`) and asserts `manifestValue.commandContracts.target.runtimeCommand === DEFINE_MOUSE_CAPTURE_POLICY_CONTRACT.runtimeCommand` and the explicit-null surface entry `{reason:'No mouse capture or release policy is visible within the 01-010 read scope.', surface:'mouse-capture-policy'}` is present. The MouseCaptureContext interface fields are all readonly + required, so undefined/null can only enter at the JS<->TS boundary (validated at runtime by `assertRuntimeCommand`'s string equality). Endianness/wrap/saturation/sign-extension N/A (declarative policy with string + boolean fields only). No silent failure path — runtime-command mismatch throws immediately.
- performance_findings: None — `defineMouseCapturePolicy` is a single boundary-check + three branches that return frozen pre-existing policy singletons. No allocations on hot path, no closures, no boxing of fixed-point or angle values. The policy map (`RELEASED_MOUSE_POLICY_BY_REASON`) is a frozen module-level constant keyed by `ReleasedMouseCaptureReason` and the captured policy is also a module-level frozen singleton. The contract metadata (`DEFINE_MOUSE_CAPTURE_POLICY_CONTRACT`) is built once at module load, not per call. The focused test reads the 01-010 manifest once and parses it once.
- improvement_findings: (1) Missing edge-case tests for focus-loss priority — the prior test suite locked focus-loss only with `inputOwner='gameplay'` and never exercised the `hasWindowFocus=false` + `inputOwner='deterministic-replay'` or `hasWindowFocus=false` + `inputOwner='menu'` cases, so the priority guarantee that focus-loss takes precedence over both the deterministic-replay and menu-active reasons was implicit and unprotected from refactor drift. (2) `assertRuntimeCommand` hardcoded the literal `'bun run doom.ts'` inside its error message instead of interpolating `EXPECTED_RUNTIME_COMMAND` and did not echo the actually-received runtime command, diverging from the sibling pattern in `src/playable/input/releaseInputOnFocusLoss.ts` that uses `requires "${EXPECTED_RUNTIME_COMMAND}". Received \`${runtimeCommand}\`.` — preserves the original substring `'defineMouseCapturePolicy requires \`bun run doom.ts\`.'` for any external matcher, but adds the received value for diagnostics and is robust to a future rename of the constant. For a 320x200 menu overlay (~64K pixels) this added redundant property accesses and multiplications inside the per-pixel hot path. Additionally the row-on-screen test (`framebufferRow < 0 || framebufferRow >= SCREENHEIGHT`) was evaluated per-pixel rather than per-row, despite being constant for the entire row.

Per-pixel counter semantics are preserved — a transparent pixel still counts only as transparent, an off-row pixel still counts as off-screen, and a both-off-screen pixel still counts as off-screen. (2) Updated the locked source SHA-256 from `02b8c231b4f5d8e8c2df97a2227a3ed0eb2ae687a3450647162f760923894c5e` to `aa043492326858b39319d161e289753d3eafa9fd4352f36c37a5c3a8edc62db9` after recomputing live with `Bun.CryptoHasher`. ## 2026-04-26T00:42:44Z - 10-003 lock-sfx-channel-count - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 10-003
- step_title: lock-sfx-channel-count
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/audio-product-integration/lockSfxChannelCount.ts` and `test/playable/audio-product-integration/lock-sfx-channel-count.test.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. `LOCK_SFX_CHANNEL_COUNT_RUNTIME_COMMAND` pins `'bun run doom.ts'`, `LOCKED_SFX_CHANNEL_COUNT` pins `8`, `SFX_CHANNEL_INDEX_MINIMUM` pins `0`, `SFX_CHANNEL_INDEX_MAXIMUM` pins `7` — all matching the vanilla `snd_channels = 8` reference (`s_sound.c` / channels.ts:75 `NUM_CHANNELS = 8`). `lockSfxChannelCount` validates the runtime command at the boundary (throws when not `'bun run doom.ts'`), validates the channel-snapshot length is exactly `LOCKED_SFX_CHANNEL_COUNT`, then walks slots `0..7` in deterministic ascending order and pre-validates each snapshot before any signature is appended: `snapshot === undefined` (sparse array hole) → throws "SFX channel slot N is missing"; `snapshot.channelIndex !== expectedChannelIndex` → throws "SFX channel index X must match slot N"; `snapshot.origin` non-null and not an integer (covers `NaN`, `Infinity`, fractional, non-number) → throws "SFX channel N origin must be an integer or null"; `snapshot.sfxId` non-null and not an integer → throws "SFX channel N sfxId must be an integer or null". The signature template `channel=N;origin=...;sfx=...` uses the `??` operator so legitimate integer `0` for origin/sfxId is preserved as `'0'` (NOT confused with `null`); `occupiedChannelCount` increments on every non-null `sfxId`. Replay evidence is built with the FNV-1a 32-bit `Math.imul`-driven checksum (offset basis `0x811c9dc5`, prime `0x01000193`, end-of-record separator `0x0a`) and a `>>> 0` final coercion to keep the result in unsigned-32-bit space. The result, the `replayEvidence`, and the `slotSignatures` array are each `Object.freeze`-locked. `deviceHandlesIncluded: false` is asserted both structurally and by the test's `JSON.stringify(result.replayEvidence)).not.toContain('handle')` substring check, locking the deterministic-replay handle-free constraint at the type and runtime levels. No silent failure path — every invalid input throws with a clear message before any state is recorded. Endianness/wrap N/A (FNV-1a uses `Math.imul + >>> 0` for 32-bit unsigned arithmetic). Sign-extension N/A (only string charcodes 0..127 enter the checksum). The test 1 cross-validates the live `plan_fps/manifests/01-011-audit-missing-live-audio.json` manifest's `commandContracts.target.runtimeCommand`, `step.id/title`, `schemaVersion`, and the `live-sfx-mixer` explicit-null surface entry. Test 2 locks the source SHA-256 `d639d060f1698e9c306a35d5a60afadb0ff52218aa46584a5ff71810c798c50e` by recomputing it live from the source file (drift detection on any future edit).
- performance_findings: None — `lockSfxChannelCount` is a snapshot-locking boundary call, not a per-frame/per-tick/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. The single-pass loop walks exactly 8 slots; per-slot work is one `validateChannelSnapshot` call (3 cheap predicates), one conditional `occupiedChannelCount` increment, and one `slotSignatures.push` of a templated string. `Object.freeze` is called twice on objects of fixed shape and once on an 8-element array — O(1) work that does not propagate to nested string primitives (strings are immutable so freezing the array is sufficient). FNV-1a checksum loop is O(total signature characters) ≈ 8 * ~30 chars = ~240 iterations; uses `Math.imul + >>> 0` (no boxing, no closures, no object churn). No closures created in the loop; no property access on hot values that should be hoisted (each `snapshot.X` is read at most twice per slot, and the access is on a small fresh object literal — V8/JSC monomorphise these trivially). Allocation budget per call: 1 result object, 1 frozen evidence object, 1 frozen array, 8 signature strings — appropriate for snapshot-frequency invocation, no opportunity for pooling without sacrificing the deterministic-replay property.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage locked the runtime command contract, the audit-manifest cross-reference, the source SHA-256 hash, the canonical 3-occupied/5-empty mixed-state replay evidence (the only fixture exercised), the wrong-command rejection, the wrong-length rejection, and the channel-index/slot mismatch at slot 7 — but did NOT cover (a) the exported `SFX_CHANNEL_INDEX_MINIMUM` and `SFX_CHANNEL_INDEX_MAXIMUM` constants (silent drift if either was ever changed away from the vanilla 0..7 range), (b) the all-empty channel table boundary (`occupied=0`, `empty=8`) including its exact `replayChecksum` and the eight uniform `null/null` signatures, (c) the all-occupied channel table boundary (`occupied=8`, `empty=0`) including its exact `replayChecksum` and the eight non-null signatures (the canonical fixture had 5 of 8 slots free, so the all-occupied accounting branch was drift-unprotected), (d) the integer `0` boundary for both `origin` and `sfxId` — the `??` operator's nullish-only semantics for the signature template were structurally correct but no test verified that legitimate `0` integers were preserved as `'0'` (NOT confused with `null`); Cross-checked against `plan_fps/manifests/01-010-audit-missing-live-input.json`: `stepId === '01-010'` and the `input-trace-recording` `explicitNullSurfaces` entry's `reason` matches the locked contract. The `recordInputTraceFormat` boundary validates: `runtimeCommand !== 'bun run doom.ts'` throws; `Number.isInteger(tic) === false || tic < 0` throws (covers `NaN`, `Infinity`, fractional, negative); `tic < previousTic` throws (locks per-tic monotonic ordering, allowing equal tics for arrival-order semantics); per-source validation throws on invalid keyboard phase, non-integer keyboard `lparam`, invalid mouse-button button label, invalid mouse-button phase label, non-integer mouse-motion deltas, scripted Doom key out of `(0, 0xff]` range, and invalid scripted Doom key phase. Keyboard scan-code translation rejects unmappable scan codes via `translateScanCode === 0` (the table fills 0 for indices outside the 0x01..0x58 vanilla `xlatekey` set; `>= SCANCODE_TABLE_SIZE` returns 0). The `extractScanCode` and `isExtendedKey` helpers pull bits 16–23 and bit 24 from the LPARAM exactly as `i_video.c` does on Win32. Empty-input boundary: `entries.length === 0` returns `lastTic: null` and zero counts (locked by new test). Each entry is `Object.freeze`-locked at construction and the entries array, header, and summary are also `Object.freeze`-locked. Exhaustiveness: the `default` switch arm uses `unsupportedSource: never` for compile-time exhaustiveness plus a runtime throw as a safety net. No silent failure path; every invalid input throws with a clear message before the entry is recorded. Endianness/wrap N/A (LPARAM extraction uses unsigned shift `>>>`); sign-extension N/A; `previousTic` initial value `-1` is correct because the first valid event must have `tic >= 0`.
- performance_findings: None warranting a code change. The function is invoked once per input event, not per frame/tick/sample/pixel/lump. Single linear pass, O(n). Per-event allocation: one frozen entry object plus minor closure-free arithmetic. The `for ... of sourceEvents.entries()` iterator allocates one tuple per event; replacing it with an index-based `for` loop would shave a small allocation but is not worth the readability cost at this scale. Minor duplicate work in the keyboard branch — `translateScanCode(lparam)` and `extractScanCode(lparam)` each shift+mask the same lparam — but `translateScanCode` lives in the `Read Only` `src/input/keyboard.ts` (cannot extract a "translate from already-extracted scancode" variant within scope), and the operation is one shift + one mask: not a meaningful hot path cost. No closures created in loops, no boxing of fixed-point or angle values, no property access on hot values to hoist.

- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/audio-product-integration/updateSfxSpatialization.ts` and `test/playable/audio-product-integration/update-sfx-spatialization.test.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. `UPDATE_SFX_SPATIALIZATION_COMMAND` pins `'bun run doom.ts'`; `UPDATE_SFX_SPATIALIZATION_CHANNEL_COUNT` pins `8` (matching vanilla `NUM_CHANNELS`); volume bounds `[0, 15]` match the vanilla `snd_SfxVolume` range. `validateRequest` enforces (a) the runtime command at the boundary, (b) `soundEffectVolume ∈ [0, 15]` integer, (c) `listenerOrigin === null || Number.isInteger(listenerOrigin)`, (d) exact 8-channel table length, and (e) per-channel: `channelIndex === expectedChannelIndex` (per-slot positional invariant), `soundEffectId === null || (Number.isInteger && >= 1)`, `origin === null || Number.isInteger`, `pitch ∈ [0, 255]` integer, `priority >= 0` integer. `normalizeOrigin(origin)` collapses `0` to `null`, matching the vanilla "no spatial source" sentinel; the spatial path runs only when `normalizedOrigin !== null && normalizedOrigin !== normalizedListenerOrigin` (i.e., the channel has a real remote origin distinct from the listener's mobj). When the spatial path runs but `channel.sourcePosition === null`, a `TypeError` with the channel index is thrown — locking the type-and-runtime invariant that a remote origin requires a 2D position. The position-equality override `sourcePosition.x === listener.x && sourcePosition.y === listener.y ? NORM_SEP : adjusted.separation` defends against the off-by-one wrap in `relativeAngle` when the source happens to overlap the listener exactly (vanilla's `S_AdjustSoundParams` would compute `rel === 0xffffffff` and pick `finesine[FINEMASK]`); this is a wrapper-level guard for two distinct mobjs at coincident positions, distinct from the outer same-origin skip. `adjustSoundParams` delegation correctly forwards `isBossMap`, `listener`, `sfxVolume`, `source` so the boss-map (`gamemap === 8`) `BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME = 15` floor is honoured. The `audibleChannelCount` increments only on `kind === 'update'`; `stoppedChannelCount` increments only on `kind === 'stop'`; `updatedChannelCount === audibleChannelCount` by construction. The replay signature template uses `:` separators with `null`/`'null'` literal keys to keep the per-slot record machine-parseable; the `checksumReplaySignature` uses a `* 131` polynomial mod `1_000_000_007` (prime) for fast deterministic hashing without 64-bit arithmetic. The result, the `mixerActions` array, and each action object are `Object.freeze`-locked. The handle-free invariant is locked structurally and via the existing `JSON.stringify(result).not.toContain('handle')` substring check. No silent failure path; every validation throws before any state mutation. Endianness/wrap N/A (string-only checksum); sign-extension N/A.
- performance_findings: None warranting a code change. The function is invoked once per `updateSounds` phase (per frame, ≤35 Hz), not per sample/pixel. Per-channel work is bounded at 8: one `validateChannel` (5 cheap predicates), one optional `adjustSoundParams` call, one frozen action allocation, one templated signature string. The `replayEntries.join('|')` allocates the joined string once, then `checksumReplaySignature` walks it character-by-character — total cost ≈ 8 × ~40 chars = ~320 charCodeAt iterations. No closures created in the loop, no boxing of fixed-point/angle values (those are confined to `adjustSoundParams`), no property access on hot values to hoist (each `channel.X` is read at most twice on a small fresh object literal). `Object.freeze` is called per action plus once on the array — appropriate for the deterministic-replay contract.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage locked the runtime command contract, the audit-manifest cross-reference, the source SHA-256 hash `86e86eabe1ad588309e6f71770f9c34a0fc0639f58e7b597492c6cbaa0817742`, the canonical four-channel mixed-state replay evidence (one no-origin, one same-origin, one remote audible, one remote inaudible), the non-Bun runtime rejection, and the missing-sourcePosition rejection without request mutation — but did NOT cover (a) the `origin: 0` normalization branch (treated as `null`, no spatial calc; signature key becomes `null`), (b) the position-equality override (`sourcePosition.x === listener.x && sourcePosition.y === listener.y → separation = NORM_SEP`), defending against the `relativeAngle` off-by-one wrap, (c) the `isBossMap: true` floor-of-15 branch keeping a far-distance source audible, (d) the `listenerOrigin: null` path where every non-null channel origin then runs the spatial calculation, (e) the per-validator rejection branches: `soundEffectVolume` out of `[0, 15]` integer (negative, > 15, fractional, NaN), `pitch` > 255, `priority < 0`, (f) the wrong-channel-count rejection symmetric to a `length === 0` boundary, (g) the per-slot channel-index mismatch — only the existing happy path and the missing-sourcePosition path were exercised, leaving the position-aware branches and the boss-map floor structurally drift-prone.
- corrective_action: Added six regression tests to `test/playable/audio-product-integration/update-sfx-spatialization.test.ts` plus a `createSingleChannelRequest` helper that pads slots 1..7 with empties for focused single-channel scenarios: (1) `normalizes origin 0 to null and skips the spatial calculation` exercises `origin: 0` with a non-null `listenerOrigin: 9` and asserts `origin: null`, `separation: 128`, full volume — locking the normalize-to-null sentinel against any future drift to `0`-as-real-origin; (2) `forces separation to NORM_SEP when source position matches listener exactly` places source at `(1024, 2048)` with listener at `(1024, 2048)` and `origin: 5` distinct from `listenerOrigin: 99`, asserting `separation: 128` (NOT the off-by-one `relativeAngle` value) — locking the wrapper-level coincident-position guard; (3) `keeps a remote source audible at long distance under boss-map floor` places source at `x: 200_000_000` with `isBossMap: true, soundEffectVolume: 15` and asserts `kind: 'update'` with `volume: 15` (NOT `kind: 'stop'`) — locking the `BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME` floor branch via `adjustSoundParams` delegation; (4) `treats listenerOrigin null as a distinct origin and runs the spatial calculation for any non-null channel origin` exercises `listenerOrigin: null` with a far-distance remote origin and asserts the channel is correctly stopped (audible-via-distance check still runs) — locking the null vs non-null listener boundary; (5) `rejects out-of-range soundEffectVolume and pitch and a negative priority` exercises -1, 16, 1.5, NaN for volume; pitch=256; priority=-1 — locking each validator's contract; (6) `rejects a wrong channel count and an out-of-order channel index` exercises a 0-length channel table and a channel at slot 0 with `channelIndex: 1` — symmetrising the existing single-direction validation. Test count rose from 5 to 11, expects from 12 to 33. No source change was needed — every audit finding was a test gap, the implementation already correctly handles each case. ## 2026-04-26T01:17:22Z - 06-006 map-mouse-buttons - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 06-006
- step_title: map-mouse-buttons
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/input/mapMouseButtons.ts` and `test/playable/input/map-mouse-buttons.test.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. The contract pins `runtimeCommand: 'bun run doom.ts'`, `auditManifestStepId: '01-010'`, `deterministicReplayCompatible: true`, `eventTypes: ['down', 'up']`, `ticCommandSize: TICCMD_SIZE` (8), and three `supportedButtons` entries whose `buttonSlot` indices match the Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` defaults (`mousebfire = 0` → 'left' = 'attack', `mousebstrafe = 1` → 'right' = 'strafe-modifier', `mousebforward = 2` → 'middle' = 'move-forward'). The `LEFT_BUTTON_ATTACK_DELTA` is built via `packTicCommand(0, 0, 0, BT_ATTACK, 0, 0)` (buttons byte = 1) and the `MIDDLE_BUTTON_FORWARD_DELTA` via `packTicCommand(FORWARD_MOVE[0], 0, 0, 0, 0, 0)` (forwardmove = 0x19 = 25, vanilla walk speed) — both routed through `packTicCommand`'s clamp-and-truncate path so the deltas are byte-deterministic and frozen. The boundary throws on `runtimeCommand !== 'bun run doom.ts'` (locked literal) and on `eventType` not in `{'down', 'up'}`; the switch returns `null` for any unknown `buttonName`; the press path returns the cached delta, the release path always returns `EMPTY_TICCMD`. No silent failure path. Endianness/wrap/sign-extension N/A — the only numerical fields are the 8-bit/16-bit slots already truncated by `packTicCommand`. **Defect identified**: post-switch `if (semanticAction === null) { return null; }` plus the initializations `let buttonSlot = -1; let semanticAction: ... | null = null; let ticCommandDelta = EMPTY_TICCMD;` were dead code — every `case` assigns non-null `semanticAction` and `default` returns null, so the post-switch null check was unreachable and the dummy initial values masked future drift if a new case were added without an assignment in any of the three slots.
- performance_findings: None — this is a once-per-event boundary call (≤ a handful per tic at most), not a per-frame/per-tick/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. Per-call work is one runtime-command compare, one event-type compare, one switch, one frozen-object allocation, and one ternary; no closures inside loops, no boxing, no property access on hot values to hoist.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage locked the contract object, the SHA-256 contract hash `508ba352f0883d069d882f50bac8d31def629c17affa01eb29086914fb34ebfe`, the 01-010 manifest cross-reference (stepId, runtimeCommand, three explicitNullSurfaces, no documented mouse control), the canonical four happy-path returns (left/right/middle press and left release), the `null` return for an unsupported button name, the non-Bun runtime rejection, and the unsupported-event-type rejection — but did NOT cover (a) `eventType: 'up'` for the 'middle' or 'right' buttons (only 'left' release was exercised, leaving the EMPTY_TICCMD-on-release semantics drift-prone for two of three button slots), (b) case-sensitivity boundary for the button name (e.g., 'Left', 'LEFT', 'Right', 'Middle' should each return null and not casefold), (c) whitespace-padded or empty button name rejection (' left', 'left ', '' should each return null), (d) empty-string `runtimeCommand` rejection, (e) empty-string `eventType` rejection (the throw should include the empty string in its message), (f) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the returned mapping (its `ticCommandDelta` is itself frozen), (g) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the contract's nested `eventTypes`/`supportedButtons` arrays and each `supportedButtons[i]` plus its `ticCommandDelta`, (h) explicit redundancy lock on the buttonSlot/buttonName mapping itself (a dedicated regression that converts the `supportedButtons` array into a Map and pins the three slot integers, so any future swap of slot indices would trip the test independently of the hash pin).
- corrective_action: Removed the dead post-switch null check and the dummy initialization values from `src/playable/input/mapMouseButtons.ts`. Replaced `let buttonSlot = -1; let semanticAction: MouseButtonSemanticAction | null = null; let ticCommandDelta = EMPTY_TICCMD;` with definite-assignment-friendly `let buttonSlot: number; let semanticAction: MouseButtonSemanticAction; let pressedDelta: TicCommand;` so TypeScript's CFA enforces every `case` arm assigning each variable (a future case that forgets one will fail typecheck). Reordered the switch arms to match buttonSlot order (0=left, 1=right, 2=middle) for readability. Renamed `ticCommandDelta` (the local) to `pressedDelta` to disambiguate it from the result field of the same name and to make the down/up ternary read as `args.eventType === 'down' ? pressedDelta : EMPTY_TICCMD`. The contract object value is byte-identical (no field added/removed/reordered), so the SHA-256 contract hash `508ba352f0883d069d882f50bac8d31def629c17affa01eb29086914fb34ebfe` is preserved verbatim — verified by re-running the existing hash-pin test. - prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/bun-runtime-entry-point/implementDefaultConfigLoading.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. `IMPLEMENT_DEFAULT_CONFIG_LOADING_CONTRACT` is a frozen `as const` literal pinning `currentEntrypoint` (path/script/source-catalog id S-FPS-011, help usage lines, command `bun run src/main.ts`), `defaultConfigurationLoading.candidatePaths === DEFAULT_CONFIGURATION_CANDIDATE_PATHS` reference equality (same readonly tuple instance, asserted via `toBe` in the focused test), `fileReader: 'Bun.file'`, `loadTiming: 'launcher-startup-before-session'`, `parser: 'whitespace-separated-doom-default-configuration-lines'`, `rejectedNodeSurfaces: ['fs', 'node:fs']`, `deterministicReplayCompatibility.gameStateMutation: 'none-before-session'`, and the target command transition (`bun run doom.ts`, status `missing-from-current-launcher-surface`). The Bun-only file reader uses `Bun.file(path).exists()` and `.text()` (no `node:fs` import). `loadDefaultConfiguration` iterates candidates, pushes each into `checkedPaths` BEFORE the existence probe (so the returned list reflects exactly which paths were probed), short-circuits on the first hit, and returns `status: 'missing'` with `entries: []` when none exists — verified across all four reachable result shapes. `parseDefaultConfigurationText` normalizes line endings via `replaceAll('\r\n', '\n').replaceAll('\r', '\n').split('\n')` (handles Windows CRLF, classic-Mac CR, and Unix LF), trims each line, skips empty lines and lines starting with `#` or `;`, finds the first whitespace separator with `/\s/.exec`, falls through to `value: ''` when no separator exists, and emits `lineNumber: lineIndex + 1` (1-based, matching vanilla `default.cfg` line numbering). The fact log at `plan_fps/FACT_LOG.md` line 24 records both `doom/default.cfg` and `doom/chocolate-doom.cfg` as live local reference assets, satisfying the candidate-path authority check. Cross-reference with `plan_fps/manifests/01-007-audit-missing-bun-run-doom-entrypoint.json` reverifies the contract's `currentEntrypoint` and `targetCommand` blocks via deep equality. No nullable/wrap-around/sign-extension boundary applies to this declarative startup-only loader.
- performance_findings: None — config loading runs once at launcher startup before session creation, never on a per-tic/per-frame/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. The `replaceAll().replaceAll().split()` chain allocates two intermediate strings per file but is amortized over a single load event. The `/\s/` literal regex inside the per-line loop is not hoisted, but V8/JavaScriptCore typically cache regex literals, and config files are O(<200) lines, so even an un-cached path is negligible. No object churn, no closures created inside loops, no boxing of fixed-point values, no blocking sync I/O — the Bun.file reader returns a Promise that resolves over the platform's async file handle.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage was strong on the contract (full `toEqual` plus SHA-256 hash a9d0aa596e667baa68a6908b5ed53a4f91deb39eb15a3c8eb138464e8dde824a, candidate-paths reference equality), audit-manifest cross-reference (currentEntrypoint, targetCommand, schemaVersion=1), package.json `start` script lock, fact-log candidate-path authority, the parser for the canonical comment + LF-separated case, the second-candidate-found path through `loadDefaultConfiguration`, and the missing-no-text-read path. Coverage gaps: (a) the FIRST-candidate-found short-circuit path was unexercised (the existing `loadDefaultConfiguration` test only hits the second candidate and would silently pass even if the loop forgot to short-circuit at index 0), (b) the parser's classic-Mac CR-only line-ending branch was unexercised (only `\n` was tested, so a regression that drops `replaceAll('\r', '\n')` would not trip), (c) tab-as-separator was unexercised (only single-space separators tested; a regression that narrows `/\s/` to a literal `' '` would not trip), (d) empty-input and whitespace-only-input paths were unexercised, (e) lines with leading whitespace before the key were unexercised (the `trim()` call at the top of each iteration is the only thing keeping these from yielding bogus empty-prefixed keys), (f) the key-without-value branch (no separator match) was only implicitly exercised through the comment-skip path.
- improvement_findings (continued): No clarity, dead-code, or naming issues found in the implementation; the `bunDefaultConfigurationFileReader` extraction with `DefaultConfigurationFileReader` interface cleanly separates the production Bun-backed path from the test fakes, so the tests inject a custom reader without touching production code or any node:fs surface.

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7

- step_id: 04-010

- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/window-host/runMessagePump.ts` and `test/playable/window-host/run-message-pump.test.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT` is wrapped in `Object.freeze` with a frozen `nativeMessageSource` sub-block pinning `closeBranch: 'if (message === WM_CLOSE) {'`, `destroyBranch: 'if (message === WM_DESTROY || message === WM_QUIT) {'`, `dispatchCall: 'void user32.symbols.DispatchMessageW(messageBuffer.ptr);'`, `messageLoop: 'while (user32.symbols.PeekMessageW(messageBuffer.ptr, 0n, 0, 0, PM_REMOVE) !== 0) {'`, `sleepCall: 'await Bun.sleep(1);'`, `translateCall: 'void user32.symbols.TranslateMessage(messageBuffer.ptr);'`. Each of these literal source fragments was cross-validated against `src/launcher/win32.ts` lines 161, 164, 170, 175, 176, and 208 — all present verbatim. `defaultClientSize` is `Object.freeze(computeClientDimensions(2, true))` which yields `{ width: 640, height: 480 }` (the inner freeze is redundant since computeClientDimensions already returns frozen, but harmless defensive pattern). `defaultScale: 2`, `idleSleepMilliseconds: 1`, `runtimeCommand: 'bun run doom.ts'`, `stepId: '04-010'`, `stepSlug: 'run-message-pump'` all match the contract. The `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT_SHA256` export is computed at module-load via `createHash('sha256').update(JSON.stringify(RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT)).digest('hex')` and produces `0bf7a9e8af73a26200d7d7ba19a3efadf9803fd3485291a121e588036896a932` against the current contract layout — locked verbatim by the new test below. The `runMessagePump(options)` boundary check `options.runtimeCommand !== RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT.runtimeCommand` rejects any non-`'bun run doom.ts'` command (including the empty string, which is the most common silent-fallback drift) with literal error message `runMessagePump only supports bun run doom.ts`. The per-message loop walks `options.queuedMessages` in order, pushing each to `processedMessages` BEFORE checking terminal status; on `WM_CLOSE` it returns immediately with `destroyWindow: true` and `terminalReason: 'window-close-requested'` (matches live source line 165 calling `DestroyWindow` then `return`); on `WM_DESTROY` or `WM_QUIT` it returns with `destroyWindow: false` and `terminalReason: 'window-quit-requested'` (matches live source line 170-173 returning without DestroyWindow because the OS already destroyed the window). Non-terminal messages are pushed to `translatedAndDispatchedMessages` after the terminal check, which preserves the live launcher's "translate-then-dispatch only the non-terminal messages" sequence — verified by the existing test where `WM_CLOSE` appears in `processedMessages` but NOT in `translatedAndDispatchedMessages`. All four return sites use `Object.freeze` over the result and `Object.freeze([...processedMessages])` / `Object.freeze([...translatedAndDispatchedMessages])` to lock the result and its arrays — verified by the new freeze-invariant regression test. The per-return spread-clones the working arrays into the result so the caller observes a stable snapshot independent of the internal accumulators. Endianness/wrap-around/saturation/sign-extension N/A (the function operates only on string identifiers and a boolean enum). No silent failure path — invalid runtime commands throw at the boundary before any state is recorded.
- performance_findings: None — `runMessagePump` is a snapshot-frequency boundary call modeling the message-pump contract decisions, not a per-frame/per-tic/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. The for-of loop walks at most as many entries as queued messages (small, typically a few dozen at most). Each return spread-clones the two working arrays — O(n) per return for n = drained messages — which is appropriate for snapshot-frequency invocation. The shared frozen `DEFAULT_CLIENT_SIZE` singleton avoids re-allocating the client-size object on every return. `Object.freeze` is called on the result and on each fresh array slice — O(1) work that does not propagate to nested string primitives (strings are immutable, so freezing the array is sufficient). No closures created in loops, no boxing of fixed-point or angle values, no property access on hot values to hoist. Allocation budget per call: 1 result object, 2 frozen array clones, plus the spread-source copies — no opportunity for pooling without sacrificing the deterministic-snapshot property the contract guarantees.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage locked the contract object via `toStrictEqual` (full structural lock against every field), the live launcher source-fragment evidence (six `toContain` assertions over `src/launcher/win32.ts`), the audit manifest cross-references (`commandContracts.targetRuntimeCommand`, `currentLauncherHostTransition.call`, `currentLauncherHostTransition.defaultScale`), the dynamic SHA-256 self-consistency check (recomputed live and compared to the export — a tautology that catches divergence between the export and the JSON stringify but does NOT lock the hash to a literal), the canonical happy-path WM_KEYDOWN+WM_MOUSEMOVE continue-running case, the WM_PAINT+WM_CLOSE close case (with destroyWindow=true), the WM_PAINT+WM_QUIT quit case (with destroyWindow=false), and the wrong-runtime-command rejection. Coverage gaps: (a) the SHA-256 hash was self-verified but never locked to a hex literal — a future contract drift would silently change the hash and the existing test would still pass against the recomputed value, leaving no canary; (b) the empty `queuedMessages` boundary (no messages in the drain → falls through to the final continue-running return with empty arrays) was never exercised, so any regression that mishandled the zero-iteration loop (e.g., not freezing the result) would slip through; (c) WM_DESTROY-specific handling was never directly tested — only WM_QUIT exercised the `'window-quit-requested'` branch, so a regression that mishandled WM_DESTROY (e.g., a typo dropping `WM_DESTROY` from the OR check) would be invisible; (d) WM_CLOSE order-priority with subsequent terminal messages was never tested — the function correctly returns at the first WM_CLOSE without processing later WM_DESTROY/WM_QUIT in the queue, but a regression that flipped the order priority or dropped the early-return would slip through; (e) the empty-string `runtimeCommand` rejection was never exercised — the most common silent drift is a default-fallback returning `''` for an unset env, and no test locked that this still throws; (f) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the contract, its `nativeMessageSource` sub-block, and its `defaultClientSize` was never asserted — the structural toStrictEqual would catch shape changes but not freeze-state regressions; (g) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the result and its `processedMessages` / `translatedAndDispatchedMessages` / `defaultClientSize` arrays/objects was never asserted, so a regression dropping any of the four `Object.freeze` calls in the return paths would slip through.

Added seven regression tests to `test/playable/window-host/run-message-pump.test.ts`: (1) `locks the contract SHA-256 to a hex literal so silent contract drift is caught` asserts `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT_SHA256 === '0bf7a9e8af73a26200d7d7ba19a3efadf9803fd3485291a121e588036896a932'` — pins the hash to a concrete literal so any future contract change must update this value, breaking the silent-drift loophole left by the self-consistency check; (2) `locks runtime-frozen invariants on the contract and every nested object` asserts `Object.isFrozen` over `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT`, `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT.nativeMessageSource`, and `RUN_MESSAGE_PUMP_CONTRACT.defaultClientSize` — independently catches any regression that drops one of the three Object.freeze calls in the contract layout; (3) `rejects an empty-string runtime command at the boundary` passes `runtimeCommand: ''` and asserts the same `runMessagePump only supports bun run doom.ts` throw — locks the strict-equality boundary check against the most common silent-fallback drift; (4) `returns continue-running with empty arrays when no messages are queued` passes `queuedMessages: []` and asserts the full `toStrictEqual` against the empty-arrays continue-running shape — locks the zero-iteration loop fall-through to the final return; - correctness_findings: Implementation in `src/playable/save-load-playability/restoreGameStateFromSave.ts` and `test/playable/save-load-playability/restore-game-state-from-save.test.ts` satisfies every Expected Changes bullet. `RESTORE_GAME_STATE_FROM_SAVE_RUNTIME_COMMAND = 'bun run doom.ts'` is the locked product command. `restoreGameStateFromSave(input)` validates inputs at the system boundary in two ordered guards: (1) `assertRuntimeCommand(command)` throws `RangeError('Restore game state from save must run through bun run doom.ts.')` for any command other than the locked product command — and the empty string is correctly rejected because `'' !== 'bun run doom.ts'` (verified by the new empty-command regression test); (2) `assertStartOffset(input.startOffset)` throws `RangeError('startOffset must be a non-negative safe integer.')` for any explicit value that is non-integer (incl. NaN, fractions, Infinity), negative, or above `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER`. The `startOffset !== undefined` short-circuit correctly skips the check when the field is omitted — locked by the new "accepts startOffset zero" boundary test. The `command ?? RESTORE_GAME_STATE_FROM_SAVE_RUNTIME_COMMAND` nullish-coalescing fallback correctly defaults a missing or null command to the locked product command — verified by the new "uses the default product command when no command field is supplied" test. The main flow has three distinct error paths: (a) `readSaveGameHeader` throws (e.g., buffer too small per `assertBufferSize`) → `'corrupted'` with `bytesRead: 0`, no header; (b) `readSaveGameHeader` returns null (version mismatch) → `'unsupported-version'` with `bytesRead: SAVEGAME_HEADER_SIZE`, no header; (c) `readLoadGame` throws (e.g., bad EOF marker, truncated archive) → `'corrupted'` with `bytesRead: SAVEGAME_HEADER_SIZE`, with the parsed header for evidence. The `result === null` branch from `readLoadGame` is dead defensive code (since we already verified `header !== null` above and `readLoadGame` is deterministic on the same input bytes), but it preserves the no-silent-failure invariant and matches the project's defensive `null` propagation pattern — left in place per CLAUDE.md's "don't refactor beyond what the task requires" guidance. The success path returns `'restored'` with the parsed header fields, the `bytesRead` and `nextOffset` propagated from `readLoadGame`'s read result, and the `playerMask` derived from the parsed `playeringame` array — verified by the new "restores a valid empty-archive savegame" test that constructs a full valid save (header + zero-player archive + empty world + empty mobjs section + empty specials section + EOF marker) and confirms the wrapper restores it with `status: 'restored'`, `description: 'RESTORE-STATE'`, `gameepisode: 1`, `gamemap: 1`, `gameskill: 2`, `leveltime: 0x004567`, `playerMask: 0`, `bytesRead === saveBytes.length`, and `nextOffset === saveBytes.length`. The `nextOffset` correctly propagates the `startOffset` parameter — verified by the new "propagates a non-zero startOffset" test that passes `startOffset: 7` and asserts `nextOffset === 7 + saveBytes.length`, cross-validated against a direct `readLoadGame(saveBytes, EMPTY_LAYOUT, 7)` call. `createReplayChecksum` uses FNV-1a 32-bit (`Math.imul + >>> 0` for unsigned wrap), with the payload joined by newline and the `?? ''` fallback preserving integer `0` correctly (verified structurally by the existing checksum-locked tests). `createByteHash` clamps `byteCount` between 0 and `source.length` so out-of-range parsed bytesRead values cannot trigger an unbounded subarray. `createPlayerMask` walks `playeringame.length` (typed as a 4-tuple, so bounded) — bit-shifts `1 << playerIndex` are safe because the shift count is always in `[0, 4)`. All return sites use `Object.freeze` on the result evidence and on the nested `transition` — verified by the new freeze-invariant regression test on both the restored and corrupted paths. Endianness/wrap-around/sign-extension N/A (the function operates on byte buffers via the underlying `readSaveGameHeader` / `readLoadGame` parsers, which already handle byte ordering in the header's leveltime field). No silent failure path — every error condition produces a deterministic frozen evidence record with a specific status enum.
- performance_findings: None — `restoreGameStateFromSave` is a one-shot user-action call (load a save, snapshot the result), not a per-frame/per-tic/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. The `Bun.CryptoHasher` allocation in `createByteHash` is a single per-call allocation; the FNV-1a `createReplayChecksum` walks one short joined string per call; the `Object.freeze` calls run on small fixed-shape objects. Underlying `readLoadGame` allocations (subarrays, frozen sections) are unavoidable for the parser's structural integrity. No closures created in loops, no boxing of fixed-point or angle values, no property access on hot values to hoist, no opportunity for pooling without sacrificing the deterministic-snapshot property.

Defect found: while the outer contract was wrapped in `Object.freeze`, the nested `currentLauncherTransition`, `deterministicReplayCompatibility`, and `titlePolicy` objects were plain literals — `Object.freeze` is shallow, so a downstream caller could mutate any of these inner objects at runtime, breaking the project's contract-immutability convention used by `handleCloseButton.ts` and `runMessagePump.ts`. The defect did not affect the locked SHA-256 hash because `JSON.stringify` ignores freeze metadata.

The FNV-1a 32-bit `calculateReplayChecksum` uses initial value `0x811c9dc5`, prime `0x01000193`, `Math.imul` for unsigned 32-bit multiply, and final `>>> 0` for unsigned wrap — produces the locked checksums `166_819_490` (restored) and `142_851_233` (skipped). The strings the checksum operates on are pure ASCII in the test fixtures (charCodeAt yields ≤127), so the 16-bit-code-unit-vs-8-bit-byte distinction does not affect output. All four nested state blocks (audioState, inputState, renderState, the result itself) wrap in `Object.freeze`. The `commandContract` reference points to the shared frozen contract singleton. `header.description`, `header.gameepisode`, `header.gamemap`, `header.gameskill`, `header.leveltime`, and `header.playeringame` are read once each and propagated verbatim into the transition signature. `createPlayerPresenceSignature` walks `header.playeringame.length` (typed as a 4-tuple, so bounded) and concatenates `String(header.playeringame[index])` — internal trust applies (the upstream `readSaveGameHeader` populates these from one byte each). Endianness/wrap-around/sign-extension N/A (the function operates on already-parsed header fields and string concatenation). No silent failure path — every error condition throws at the boundary with a literal product-command error message. No defects found in the source.
- performance_findings: None — `restorePostLoadRenderAudioInputState` is a one-shot user-action call (load a save, finalize post-load deterministic state), not a per-frame/per-tic/per-sample/per-pixel hot path. Per-call cost is one strict-equality command compare, one nullability branch on `options.header`, six string template interpolations for the transition signature, one FNV-1a checksum walk over a short ASCII string, and four `Object.freeze` calls over small fixed-shape objects. No closures created in loops, no boxing of fixed-point or angle values, no property access on hot values to hoist, no opportunity for pooling without sacrificing the deterministic-snapshot property the contract guarantees.
- improvement_findings: Pre-existing test coverage locked the runtime command and command contract via `toBe` and `toEqual`, the source SHA-256 hash literal `68d6447cf1a31a54bc8e575438941265ed1202c7528325f70ac06f029e8fc9af` (catches any drift in the source bytes), the canonical restored happy path (full result `toEqual` including replayChecksum 166_819_490 and the locked transitionSignature), the canonical skipped path (full result `toEqual` including replayChecksum 142_851_233), the wrong-command rejection (`'bun run src/main.ts'` → throw), and the audit manifest text-substring cross-references (`schemaVersion: 1`, `runtimeCommand: 'bun run doom.ts'`, `surface: 'live-load-game-roundtrip'`, `'post-load state handling'`, plus `SAVEGAME_VERSION_TEXT === 'version 109'`). Coverage gaps: (a) the empty-string `command: ''` rejection was never tested — `'' !== 'bun run doom.ts'` is structurally correct but no test locked this against silent-fallback drift, and the audit-pattern peers (`runMessagePump`, `restoreGameStateFromSave`) had recently added the same regression test for the identical drift class; (b) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the result and its nested `audioState`/`inputState`/`renderState`/`commandContract` was never asserted on either the restored or the skipped path — `toEqual` is structural and does NOT detect freeze-state regressions, so a regression dropping any of the four `Object.freeze` calls in `createRestoredResult` or `createSkippedResult` would silently slip through; (c) the `Object.isFrozen` invariant on the shared `RESTORE_POST_LOAD_RENDER_AUDIO_INPUT_STATE_COMMAND_CONTRACT` singleton was never asserted, so a regression dropping the `Object.freeze` wrap on the contract literal would silently allow downstream callers to mutate the singleton.
- corrective_action: Source unchanged (no defects to fix; the locked source SHA-256 hash `68d6447cf1a31a54bc8e575438941265ed1202c7528325f70ac06f029e8fc9af` is preserved and the focused test's `calculateSourceHash` lock against the literal continues to pass). Added four regression tests to `test/playable/save-load-playability/restore-post-load-render-audio-input-state.test.ts`: (1) `rejects an empty-string command at the boundary so silent fallback drift cannot bypass the runtime check` exercises both `command: ''` with the loaded header AND `command: ''` with `header: null` and asserts the same `'restore post-load render/audio/input state requires bun run doom.ts.'` throw — locks the strict-equality boundary against silent-fallback drift on both branches of the function; (2) `returns a frozen restored evidence whose nested audio render and input states are also frozen` invokes the restored happy path and asserts `Object.isFrozen` over `result`, `result.audioState`, `result.commandContract`, `result.inputState`, `result.renderState` — independently catches any regression dropping any of the freeze calls in `createRestoredResult`; (3) `returns a frozen skipped evidence whose nested audio render and input states are also frozen` mirrors test (2) on the skipped path — independently catches the same freeze regressions in `createSkippedResult`; (4) `keeps the shared command contract object frozen so callers cannot mutate it` asserts `Object.isFrozen(RESTORE_POST_LOAD_RENDER_AUDIO_INPUT_STATE_COMMAND_CONTRACT)` — independently catches a regression dropping the contract-singleton freeze. Test count rose from 5 to 9, expect calls from 11 to 24.
