## 2026-04-26T02:55:00Z - 10-001 select-and-open-bun-win32-audio-host - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 10-001
- step_title: select-and-open-bun-win32-audio-host
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: REAL DEFECT — partial-open handle leak. Original implementation in src/playable/audio-product-integration/selectAndOpenBunWin32AudioHost.ts opened music then sfx via two sequential openAudioDevice calls; if openDevice('music') succeeded and then openDevice('sfx') threw (or the sfx receipt failed validateOpenReceipt with wrong role / empty deviceName / handle <= 0n), the function threw without ever surfacing the music receipt to the caller, so the music device handle was permanently lost. CLAUDE.md FFI rules require every Open*/Create* paired with a Close* in finally; this surface owns the receipts between open and the function's return, so the open/close pairing rule applies even though the immediate FFI lives in the injected opener. validateOpenReceipt also dereferenced receipt.deviceName.length and compared receipt.handle <= 0n without typeof guards, so a receipt where deviceName was undefined would TypeError at .length and a receipt where handle was undefined would silently pass `<=0n` (`undefined <= 0n` is false) — both pass-throughs of malformed receipts.
- performance_findings: Function is called once per startup; no per-frame/per-tick path. The original allocation of `Object.freeze<BunWin32AudioHostDeviceRole[]>(['music', 'sfx'])` inside the function on every call has been hoisted to a module-level SELECTED_ROLES const for one-time allocation; the audit-time savings is symbolic for a once-per-process function but matches the codebase convention for static role lists.
- improvement_findings: Tests covered only the happy path, runtime-command rejection, and the source-hash drift guard (4 tests, 15 expects). Missing: wrong platform rejection, negative/fractional/NaN/Infinity openedAtTic, invalid bufferSampleCount/channelCount/sampleRateHz overrides, undefined-override fallback to defaults, partial-open cleanup paths, closer-failure swallowing, Object.isFrozen on result/liveDevices/replayEvidence/selection/each device, and the validators for empty deviceName / non-positive handle / wrong role from the opener (every clause of validateOpenReceipt was untested).
- corrective_action: (a) Added optional `closeDevice: BunWin32AudioHostDeviceCloser` to SelectAndOpenBunWin32AudioHostRequest plus an exported BunWin32AudioHostDeviceCloser type. (b) Refactored the open path to push every receipt onto an `opened: BunWin32AudioHostDeviceOpenReceipt[]` *before* validateOpenReceipt, then wrap the for-of loop in try/catch; on any throw the catch calls closeOpenedDevices(opened, request.closeDevice) which iterates every opened receipt and calls closer (if provided) inside its own try/catch so closer failures are swallowed and the original error is re-thrown. This guarantees: (i) no handle is ever lost when a later open or validation throws, (ii) closer errors never mask the original failure, (iii) calling without closeDevice is still legal and behaves exactly as before for the success path. (c) Hardened validateOpenReceipt with `typeof receipt.deviceName === 'string'` and `typeof receipt.handle === 'bigint'` guards before the length/comparison clauses, preserving the existing error messages so undefined/non-string/non-bigint values produce the documented errors instead of TypeError or silent pass-through. (d) Hoisted SELECTED_ROLES to a module-level frozen const reused both by the open loop and by the replayEvidence.selectedRoles field. (e) Updated the source SHA-256 in the focused test from 142bf48061edc02611dd7ca45420fc7f8a9b44e65bea2d79492154b57edd9739 to c54b69b523fd7cd2a15ebd1087ae51a0f5474215d111c2760905d288b8e53e4a (post-format hash, recomputed live via Bun.CryptoHasher). (f) Added Object.isFrozen assertions on result/result.liveDevices/result.replayEvidence/result.selection and each device in liveDevices to lock the freeze contract. (g) Added 10 new tests: wrong platform rejection, openedAtTic sweep over [-1, 1.5, NaN, +Infinity], override sweep over [bufferSampleCount/channelCount/sampleRateHz × invalid values] with exact error messages, undefined-override fallback to defaults, wrong-role-from-opener with prior music close (closedReceipts === [0x2002n, 0x1001n]), empty-deviceName receipt with prior music close (closedReceipts roles === ['music', 'sfx']), zero-handle receipt with prior music close, openDevice throwing on sfx with closeDevice provided (closes only music), openDevice throwing without closeDevice (still re-throws and never returns partial), and a closer that throws (the original error survives). Test count grew from 4 to 14; expects from 15 to 52.

Pre-fix source SHA-256 a148f72dba044994bc8c081300a99a11e5d8c40c5f46a1d92d5e4fbc214f848a recomputed live via Bun.CryptoHasher and matched the test's pinned constant. DEFECT — dead-code/inconsistent-contract: `loop?: MainLoop` was an optional field on WireLevelExitFlowOptions with no caller anywhere in the repo (verified via grep across src/, test/, tools/, plan_fps/) and no test exercising the branch. The implementation guarded with `if (!loop.started) loop.setup(...)` so a caller passing a started MainLoop would skip the pre-loop sequence entirely, producing a result with `preLoopTrace: []` while every other field of the contract still advertised the canonical pre-loop steps — a silent contract leak: the result type promises `readonly preLoopTrace: readonly PreLoopStep[]` but the contract is implicitly conditional on the optional input mode. Sibling Bun-only wiring functions (wireDeathRebornFlow.ts, wireIntermissionAndFinaleTransitions.ts) do not expose this option and instead create `new MainLoop()` internally, so the dual-mode path was inconsistent with the convention.
- performance_findings: none — wireLevelExitFlow runs once per level-exit transition, not on a per-frame/per-tick path. The two createLauncherSession calls (once for current, once for next) and renderLauncherFrame are inherent costs of the contract; phaseTrace and preLoopTrace each allocate a 4-element array via the spread copy on the way out, which is intentional (snapshot semantics). No allocation in hot loops. Storing the full Uint8Array reference in flowEvidence.displayedFramebuffer was symbolic — only its byteLength was ever read — so the post-fix tracks framebufferByteLength directly for one fewer reference held across the closure boundary, which is a clarity win rather than a measurable perf win.
- improvement_findings: (1) `loop?: MainLoop` was unused dead code with the inconsistent-contract behavior above and no test coverage for either the unstarted-passed-in or started-passed-in branches. (2) flowEvidence held both `displayedFramebuffer: Uint8Array | null` and the byte-length consumer logic, with the framebuffer read only to extract byteLength — direct tracking of framebufferByteLength removes the unused intermediate. (3) Existing tests had three coverage gaps inside step scope: case-insensitive normalizeMapName (lowercase/mixed-case input → uppercase) was not directly tested even though the implementation calls `.toUpperCase()`; the empty-name rejection branch of normalizeMapName was unreachable from any existing test (no test sets currentMapName='' or nextMapName=''); no Object.isFrozen assertion existed on the result or any of its sub-objects (commandContract, levelTime, phaseTrace, preLoopTrace, transition), so a regression dropping any Object.freeze would ship silently as long as the structural toEqual still matched.
- corrective_action: (a) Removed the dead `loop?: MainLoop` field from WireLevelExitFlowOptions and the corresponding `options.loop ?? new MainLoop()` plus `if (!loop.started)` branch from the function body — the implementation now always constructs a fresh MainLoop and always runs setup, eliminating the dual-mode contract leak; the result type's preLoopTrace promise is now unconditional. The `MainLoop` import remains because the construction is now internal-only. (b) Replaced flowEvidence's `displayedFramebuffer: Uint8Array | null` slot with `framebufferByteLength: number` directly populated inside display, dropping the stale Uint8Array reference and one branch of the post-loop null check (only `transition === null` remains for type narrowing through the closure boundary). (c) Removed the now-unused `LauncherSession` type import since flowEvidence.activeSession's type is inferred via `ReturnType<typeof createLauncherSession>` to keep the existing inline-type pattern. (d) Added three new focused tests, each driven through the public wireLevelExitFlow surface and the loaded DOOM1.WAD: 'normalizes lowercase and mixed-case map names to uppercase before validating availability' submits currentMapName='e1m1', nextMapName='E1m2' and asserts the result's currentMapName/nextMapName/renderedMapName/transition all carry the uppercase form, locking the .toUpperCase() normalization across both inputs; 'rejects empty current and next map name overrides' submits currentMapName='' and nextMapName='' separately and asserts each throws the literal 'map name must not be empty' message, locking the empty-string branch of normalizeMapName for both inputs; 'deep-freezes the result and its replay-evidence sub-objects' asserts Object.isFrozen on the outer result, commandContract, levelTime, phaseTrace, preLoopTrace, and transition, locking the freeze contract against silent regressions. (e) Updated the source SHA-256 in the focused test from a148f72dba044994bc8c081300a99a11e5d8c40c5f46a1d92d5e4fbc214f848a to 6b8b6b5ec40c6808832370204a98e6b2ccbf04374afba7bc19cf4bfa380c4725 (post-format hash, recomputed live via Bun.CryptoHasher). Test count grew from 5 to 8; expects from 11 to 23.

Type-level: the original ScriptedPickupFixture used `Record<string, string | number>` for trace records and existed alongside two custom assert helpers (assertScriptedPickupFixture and assertSideBySideReplayManifest) that performed only loose existence checks via toBeDefined()/Array.isArray, redundant with the tighter `toEqual(expectedFixture)` pattern used by sibling 02-021 / 02-020.

(a) Replaced the loose Record-based fixture type with a typed `ScriptedPickupPathOracleFixture` interface plus discrete CaptureCommand / CaptureWindow / ExpectedTraceEntry / InheritedSourceHash / PendingLiveHash / SourceAuthority types; ExpectedTraceEntry's phase is now the literal union `'startup' | 'title' | 'menu' | 'gameplay'`, and pendingLiveHash kind is `'audio' | 'framebuffer' | 'state'` / status is `'pending'`. (b) Introduced a single source-of-truth `expectedFixture` declared with `satisfies ScriptedPickupPathOracleFixture` so future drift in either the JSON or the type triggers a TypeScript error. (c) Replaced both custom assert helpers with the simpler `expect(Bun.file(fixturePath).json()).resolves.toEqual(expectedFixture)` lock that drops loose narrowing and gains exact structural equality on every field. (f) Replaced the cross-check helper to row-match the SOURCE_CATALOG.md table by `splitlines.find(line => line.startsWith('| <id> |'))` then assert that same row contains the authority and path strings, eliminating the false-positive across-row match. (g) Tightened the pendingLiveHashes test to assert dedupe of the kind values via Set size, lock entry.status='pending', and assert non-empty reason. (h) Added a new test 'matches the inherited launch-surface hashes against live source files' that loads the three current launch-surface files via Bun.file(...).bytes(), recomputes SHA-256 with Bun.CryptoHasher, and asserts it matches the recorded hash AND that fileBytes.byteLength matches the recorded sizeBytes — directly mirroring the 02-021 sibling pattern and turning silent manifest-staleness into a focused-test failure. JSON.stringify on the replayPayload is deterministic because every nested object uses non-integer string keys with explicit insertion order (commandContract is frozen, EMPTY_DEMO_PLAYBACK_SCRIPT is frozen with `Object.freeze([])` events, parsedDemoEvidence is constructed in alphabetical key order, transition is constructed in alphabetical key order). No nullable/empty-buffer leak — `parseDemo(Buffer.alloc(0))` throws `Demo buffer must contain at least 1 byte` and propagates to the caller, which is the documented contract for the parser boundary.
- performance_findings: none — `JSON.stringify(ticCommands)` allocates a per-tic string and the `${replayedTicCount}:${ticSignature}\n` template literal allocates one more string before hashing, but this is a one-shot determinism harness invoked from tests/CI rather than a per-frame runtime path. The hasher is updated incrementally so the full 5026-tic hash never materializes. No object churn, no closures inside the loop, no boxing.
- improvement_findings: (1) Test coverage gap — the existing `rejects demo1 playback without tic commands` test exercises the empty-tics path but no test exercised the empty-buffer path where `parseDemo(Buffer.alloc(0))` throws at the parser boundary, leaving the runtime-command guard's ordering relative to the parser undocumented for future readers. (2) The `expect(Object.isFrozen(evidence)).toBe(true)` assertion only checks the outer shell, masking any future regression that left a nested object mutable (transition, parsedDemo, finalSnapshot, initialSnapshot, postCompletionSnapshot, plus their playersInGame arrays were all already frozen via composition but no test pinned that invariant). (3) No idempotence assertion — the function is pure-by-construction, but a regression that introduced a Date.now() / Math.random() / process-counter into the hash would have gone undetected.
- corrective_action: Added three regression tests inside the existing `replayDemo1Deterministically` describe block: (a) `rejects an empty demo buffer at the parser boundary` calls with `Buffer.alloc(0)` and asserts the parser-level `Demo buffer must contain at least 1 byte` throw (ordering: runtime-command guard runs first, so the default command lets the parser throw); (b) `produces an idempotent replay hash on repeated invocations` calls with DEMO1_FIXTURE twice and asserts equal `replayHash`, equal `ticCommandHash`, and structural `toEqual`; (c) `deep-freezes every nested evidence object` asserts `Object.isFrozen` on evidence and on commandContract, demoPlaybackScript, finalSnapshot, finalSnapshot.playersInGame, parsedDemo, parsedDemo.playersInGame, transition, transition.initialSnapshot (and its playersInGame), transition.postCompletionSnapshot (and its playersInGame). No production source changes — the locked source SHA-256 (8bc1c0dd…) remains valid. Test count grew from 5 (15 expects) to 8 (27 expects).

- step_id: 11-004
- step_title: wire-bun-native-save-read-write
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: wireBunNativeSaveReadWrite satisfies every Expected Changes bullet — `assertRuntimeCommand` rejects non-`bun run doom.ts` callers BEFORE any I/O or path validation, `assertSaveFilePath` rejects empty strings and embedded NUL bytes (the rejected-path test confirms `Bun.file(path).exists() === false` after the throw), the read path streams the file via `Bun.file(...).arrayBuffer()` then wraps in Uint8Array, the write path performs a defensive `copyBytes(request.bytes)` so post-call mutation of the caller's buffer cannot retro-corrupt the on-disk bytes or the evidence (Bun.write resolves before any further mutation could occur), the FNV-1a `checksumText` uses `0x811c_9dc5` offset basis and `0x0100_0193` prime with `>>> 0` truncation matching standard 32-bit FNV-1a, and the SHA-256 hash + replay signature pin both the byte content and the parsed header fields. The 24-bit big-endian leveltime survives roundtrip (write `(0x010203 >>> 16) & 0xff = 0x01 / 0x02 / 0x03`, read `(0x01<<16) | (0x02<<8) | 0x03 = 66051`). Header-too-small inputs surface `header: null` and `versionMatches: false` without forging fields. Boundary review: empty Uint8Array writes a 0-byte file with header=null; non-existent file on read throws ENOENT (not tested but acceptable system-boundary error).
- performance_findings: `readHeaderOrNull(bytes)` was called TWICE per operation — once in the public function (so the returned `header` is correct) and again inside `createEvidence` when computing replay-signature header fields. Each call iterates through 16 version-string bytes, allocates a frozen 4-element playeringame array, and freezes a 6-field SaveGameHeader. Doubling those allocations and reads on every save read/write is unjustified for a function whose return shape exposes both `header` and `evidence.header*` from the same source bytes.
- improvement_findings: (1) Redundant header parse described above. (2) Test coverage gap — no test covered the bytes-shorter-than-SAVEGAME_HEADER_SIZE path where `readHeaderOrNull` returns null and evidence's header* fields all become null with `versionMatches: false` and `replaySignature` ends with `;header=null`. (3) No frozen-result assertion — the implementation `Object.freeze`s both write/read result objects and the evidence inside, but no test pinned that invariant against future regressions.
- corrective_action: Threaded the existing single `header` from each endpoint into `createEvidence(operation, bytes, header)` as a third parameter, removing the duplicate `readHeaderOrNull(bytes)` call inside `createEvidence`. The visible contract is unchanged — same SHA-256, same FNV-1a checksum, same replaySignature byte-for-byte (the unit test's `2320186261` write checksum and `2481476530` read checksum still hold). Source SHA-256 updated from `b3b8708c715af26ae709e54c5117a8b4d33cbf935f412c5ea92c95fdd0b4b82e` to `234520c64c1562996be327248e46ea9805dbfabc6c9c9127e6687596067e529f` (recomputed via `Bun.CryptoHasher` on the Biome-formatted source). Added two regression tests: (a) `writes byte buffers shorter than the save header without forging a header` writes `[0x00, 0x11, 0x22]`, asserts `bytesWritten === 3`, `header === null`, all evidence header fields null, `versionMatches: false`, and the literal replaySignature `operation=write;byteLength=3;hashSha256=26320e0ae7028efb6bf710654a0ed53cfcae1e5ca1e7f69d8a9dce02cfac2960;header=null` (hash recomputed live via Bun.CryptoHasher and pinned); (b) `returns frozen results and frozen evidence for both operations` performs a write then a read against the same path and asserts `Object.isFrozen` on both outer results and both inner evidence objects. Test count grew from 5 (16 expects) to 7 (29 expects).

## 2026-04-26T04:42:12Z - 09-012 render-wipe-transition-effects - Claude Code

- status: completed
- agent: Claude Code
- model: claude-opus-4-7
- effort: max
- step_id: 09-012
- step_title: render-wipe-transition-effects
- prior_audits: none
- correctness_findings: renderWipeTransitionEffects satisfies every Expected Changes bullet — `validateCommand` rejects non-`bun run doom.ts` callers BEFORE any framebuffer mutation (the rejected-command test confirms the destinationFramebuffer is byte-for-byte unchanged via `originalDestinationFramebuffer = destinationFramebuffer.slice()` snapshot), `validateFramebufferLength` rejects any of the three framebuffers whose length differs from `SCREENWIDTH * SCREENHEIGHT = 64_000`, `validateColumnRevealedRows` rejects column arrays whose length is not 320 or whose entries are non-integer / negative / `> SCREENHEIGHT` (the columnRevealedRows[12] = 201 test confirms validation fires before any mutation). The melt loop is column-major (matching vanilla `wi_stuff` melt direction) and each column reveals the top `revealedRows` rows from `endFramebuffer` and the remaining `SCREENHEIGHT - revealedRows` rows from `startFramebuffer`, mutating `destinationFramebuffer[rowIndex * 320 + columnIndex]` in place. The 32-bit FNV-1a `framebufferChecksum` uses offset basis `0x811c9dc5` and prime `0x01000193` with `Math.imul` and `>>> 0` truncation, producing the locked checksum `3_513_728_293` for the partial-melt fixture and the locked SHA-256 `701714d5e2a9fd72f13b2fcd77306ed12c14e9c58e5dfd0fc6984ee13b7f309c` for the destinationFramebuffer after the partial-melt apply. Boundary review: revealedRows === 0 short-circuits the top loop (all 200 rows from startFramebuffer); revealedRows === SCREENHEIGHT (200) short-circuits the bottom loop (all 200 rows from endFramebuffer, full reveal); changedPixelCount counts byte differences regardless of which source the byte came from.
- performance_findings: (1) The inner per-pixel loop performed two property accesses on `context` per pixel (one of `context.endFramebuffer` / `context.startFramebuffer` plus `context.destinationFramebuffer`) and one on `context.columnRevealedRows` per column — for a 64_000-pixel single call that is up to 128_000 V8 property loads that the JIT may or may not hoist. (2) `framebufferOffset = rowIndex * SCREENWIDTH + columnIndex` recomputed a multiplication and an add per pixel even though the offset advances by exactly `SCREENWIDTH` from one row to the next within a column — an accumulator avoids 64_000 multiplies. (3) `sourceByte = rowIndex < revealedRows ? endFramebuffer[off] : startFramebuffer[off]` placed a per-pixel branch inside the inner loop even though the predicate flips at most once per column — splitting the inner loop into a top section reading from `endFramebuffer` and a bottom section reading from `startFramebuffer` removes the branch entirely. (4) `revealedPixelCount += 1` ran inside the inner loop guarded by `rowIndex < revealedRows`, accumulating one pixel at a time — replacing it with `revealedPixelCount += revealedRows` once per column saves up to 64_000 increments per call.
- improvement_findings: All four perf findings above are also clarity wins — splitting the inner loop into top/bottom sections reads more clearly than a per-pixel ternary, the framebufferOffset accumulator surfaces the column-stride access pattern, and aggregating revealedPixelCount per column matches the mathematical definition. Test coverage was already strong (full reveal, partial reveal with locked SHA-256, command rejection with byte-snapshot guard, validation rejection with byte-snapshot guard) — no test additions needed.
- corrective_action: Hoisted `context.columnRevealedRows`, `context.destinationFramebuffer`, `context.endFramebuffer`, `context.startFramebuffer` into local consts immediately after validation. Replaced `revealedPixelCount += 1` (inside the inner loop) with `revealedPixelCount += revealedRows` (once per column). Replaced the unified inner row loop with two sequential loops: rows `[0, revealedRows)` read from `endFramebuffer` and rows `[revealedRows, SCREENHEIGHT)` read from `startFramebuffer`, both using a `framebufferOffset` accumulator initialized to `columnIndex` and incremented by `SCREENWIDTH` per row (eliminating the per-pixel multiply, the per-pixel ternary, and one of the per-pixel context property loads). All observable outputs are byte-for-byte preserved — the locked partial-melt result stays at `changedPixelCount: 63_792`, `revealedPixelCount: 26_560`, `framebufferChecksum: 3_513_728_293`, `complete: false`, and the destinationFramebuffer SHA-256 stays `701714d5…`; the full-reveal test still produces `complete: true` with `revealedPixelCount === FRAMEBUFFER_BYTE_LENGTH` and `destinationFramebuffer.toEqual(endFramebuffer)`. Source SHA-256 updated from `4f09303ba2e996c41045243162636874d80116ff36744c2e56e667751de21473` to `9cf4979c4e94594078f7cf8502bcc2b90bfe7f79efb079afa78c12d94cb5c544` (recomputed via `Bun.CryptoHasher` on the Biome-formatted source).

The replay checksum uses 32-bit FNV-1a (offset basis 0x811c9dc5, prime 0x01000193) with `Math.imul`+`>>> 0` truncation and an explicit zero-byte content separator that produces the locked checksum 574854910 for the documented overrides. No nullable, negative, zero, empty-buffer, wrap-around, sign-extension, or endianness boundary issue surfaced.
- performance_findings: none — `writeConfigBack` is a one-shot writeback (not per-frame, per-tic, per-sample, per-pixel, or per-lump). Two `Bun.write` calls per invocation are fundamental to the operation; sequential await preserves a deterministic ordering between two distinct files, and parallelism would save microseconds at most for two ~1–2 KiB writes. `TextEncoder` is hoisted to a module-level constant; `Bun.CryptoHasher` is allocated twice per call which is appropriate for an off-hot-path operation.
- improvement_findings: Test coverage gap — the implementation iterates `READ_ONLY_REFERENCE_ROOTS = ['doom', 'iwad', 'reference']` but only the `doom/` rejection path was locked by the test suite, leaving the `iwad/` and `reference/` branches drift-unprotected; the `lineEnding` option on `WriteConfigBackOptions` exposes a `'\\n' | '\\r\\n'` contract but no test exercised the Windows (`\\r\\n`) branch, so a regression that fell back to `\\n` regardless of the configured ending would have passed the existing suite; the empty-path and NUL-character path-validation branches inside `resolveWritableConfigPath` were also untested. The implementation source itself is internally consistent (the `^= 0x00` content-boundary XOR is a meaningful documentation marker for the FNV-1a content separator even though XOR-with-zero is mathematically a no-op — the post-content `Math.imul` carries the actual separator effect, so removing the XOR alone would not change behavior; named constants for the FNV magic numbers would be a stylistic improvement but inflating abstraction beyond what the audit requires); no source change is warranted, preserving the locked source SHA-256.

Test count grew from 5 (19 expects) to 8 (35 expects). This is a one-shot audit-helper call (not per-frame, per-tic, per-sample, per-pixel, or per-lump), so the dual-pass pattern is acceptable. The internal `let tickedDuringPhase = null` plus inline callback object allocation per call is fine for one-shot use. No per-frame allocations or boxing/unboxing of Fixed/Angle values appear on this path.
- improvement_findings: Test file test/playable/game-session-wiring/wire-world-thinker-ticking.test.ts called `await loadLauncherResources('doom/DOOM1.WAD')` inside both the 'advances one world thinker tic' and 'rejects non-target runtime commands' tests, parsing the WAD header/directory/PLAYPAL/render resources twice — the IWAD load is the dominant cost (≈40 ms each). Sibling test test/playable/game-session-wiring/wire-player-spawn-session.test.ts already uses the `beforeAll` hoist with a top-level `let launcherResources: LauncherResources` to share the load across tests, establishing the idiomatic pattern for this directory. The duplicate load is wasted work and the inconsistency is a clarity gap.
- corrective_action: Added `import { beforeAll, ... }` and `import type { LauncherResources }` to test/playable/game-session-wiring/wire-world-thinker-ticking.test.ts; introduced top-level `let launcherResources: LauncherResources` plus `beforeAll(async () => { launcherResources = await loadLauncherResources('doom/DOOM1.WAD'); })`; replaced the per-test `await loadLauncherResources(...)` calls in both world-tic tests with `launcherResources`, dropped the now-unneeded `async` modifier from each since `createLauncherSession` and `wireWorldThinkerTicking` are synchronous. No production source change; pinned source SHA-256 stays locked. Test runtime dropped from 145 ms → 120 ms (single WAD load).

For setBlocks=11 low-detail, the implementation copies the full 320*200 framebuffer through scaledViewWidth/viewHeight (not viewWidth) so the on-screen pixel coverage is correct regardless of detail-shift sampling rate. No nullable/empty/wrap-around boundary issue: framebuffer-length guard makes every indexed read safe; viewport-clamp keeps loops in-bounds. JIT may hoist some of these, but explicit hoisting reduces dependence on speculative optimizations and matches the pattern used in src/launcher/gameplayRenderer.ts (e.g. `const ceilingClip = ctx.renderState.ceilingClip;`).

Liang-Barsky clipping in clipLineToTarget is mathematically correct: for line P(t)=start+t*delta, edge constraints encode (1) startX-target.x with denominator -deltaX yielding factor=(target.x-startX)/deltaX which clips at left edge; (2) targetRight-startX with denominator deltaX yielding factor=(targetRight-startX)/deltaX clipping at right edge; (3) startY-target.y with denominator -deltaY for top; (4) targetBottom-startY with denominator deltaY for bottom — all four edges where targetRight=target.x+target.width-1 and targetBottom=target.y+target.height-1 (last-pixel-inclusive convention) match writeAutomapPixel's `x>=target.x+target.width` exclusive bounds check. Vertical/horizontal denominator==0 path correctly returns null only when numerator<0 (point fully outside that axis-aligned half-plane), continues otherwise. The early-exit predicates `factor > maximumFactor` (denominator<0) and `factor < minimumFactor` (denominator>0) correctly detect non-overlap; the Math.min/Math.max accumulation cannot drive minimumFactor above 1 or maximumFactor below 0 without first triggering an early exit. projectLine maps world (line.endX-minX) * (target.width-1) / worldWidth so endX=worldBounds.maxX maps to target.x+target.width-1 (last column) and endX=worldBounds.minX maps to target.x (first column); the Y axis is correctly inverted via (worldBounds.maxY-line.endY) so world-up becomes screen-down. drawLine's linear interpolation samples steps+1 pixels with Math.round(start + delta*k/steps) for k in [0..steps]; the deltaX==deltaY==0 case writes a single pixel via the dedicated branch. writeAutomapPixel's exclusive `x>=target.x+target.width` clamp matches the Liang-Barsky inclusive-right-edge clip exactly. clippedLineCount counts both fully-rejected lines (clippedLine===null) and partially-clipped lines (any endpoint differs after rounding); for fully-inside lines with integer projection, factor=0/factor=1 round-trips back to original endpoints exactly so no false positives. Framebuffer FNV-1a checksum (seed 0x811c9dc5, prime 0x01000193) is bit-exact for Uint8Array values 0-255; `Math.imul(...)` followed by `>>> 0` correctly produces unsigned 32-bit. countChangedPixels iterates all 64000 pixels comparing originalFramebuffer (slice taken BEFORE fill) vs current framebuffer. Cross-checked plan_fps/manifests/01-012-audit-missing-live-rendering.json: schemaVersion=1, surface 'automap-renderer-implementation' is in explicitNullSurfaces with rationale 'No automap renderer implementation path is exposed by the 01-012 read scope', commandContracts.target.runtimeCommand='bun run doom.ts' — manifest schema and command contract are both locked by the focused test via toContain assertions. Edge cases manually verified: (1) line entirely outside target → clipLineToTarget returns null → clippedLineCount++; (2) degenerate single-point line inside target → drawLine writes 1 pixel via steps==0 branch; (3) line ending exactly at boundary → clipping clamps to last valid column; (4) empty lines array → projectedLines=[] → no draws → drawnPixelCount=0; (5) overlay mode + setBlocks=11 → viewport=full screen but no fill (correct DOOM behavior); (6) line color matches background in full mode → fill changes pixels first, line redraws same color → mask increment but pixel already counted via fill change. Function is currently a planned product-surface entry under src/playable/rendering-product-integration/ with no runtime callers (verified by grep across src — only test imports), matching the same pattern as sibling steps 09-001 through 09-007 / 09-009; AGENTS.md `playable/` policy permits unwired product-surface contracts. Six tests pass (locked source SHA-256 00cd8fb0d216ccca9264d9fd73ee57ddfd6c79974008e237dd31e9a57c9dfb8b, EXPECTED_FULL_FRAMEBUFFER_SHA256 b9ee93bde164ad96c9bc7a0632df9c0113e1d4fdfc3c971104d57f15fc37810d, EXPECTED_OVERLAY_FRAMEBUFFER_SHA256 9201be8e679cdc4a8276b49f1369b3d4421ff16079dd453971e22dc7566a665b, plus FNV-1a checksums 762_377_189 / 3_890_817_733 cross-locking the same byte sequences via two independent hash families).
- performance_findings: minor (acceptable) — `input.framebuffer.slice()` allocates a 64,000-byte snapshot every call and `new Uint8Array(FRAMEBUFFER_PIXEL_COUNT)` allocates a second 64,000-byte mask; with the function not currently wired into any frame loop or hot path (zero non-test callers in src/), the per-call cost is paid only by the focused test and any future caller. countChangedPixels iterates the full 64,000-pixel framebuffer once; for overlay mode this could be reduced to iteration over only the linePixelMask-marked pixels (256 in the focused test), but the current full-scan approach is necessary for full-mode background-fill change accounting and remains O(N) where N is the fixed 64K framebuffer. drawLine uses one float division `(deltaX * stepIndex) / steps` per pixel inside the inner loop; switching to incremental Bresenham (matching the vanilla AM_drawFline reference noted in src/ui/automap.ts:71-78) would eliminate the divisions but requires updating the locked source SHA-256 and would alter pixel ordering in deep edge cases. Validation iterates input.lines once via for-of without allocations. No allocations inside the line-drawing inner loop. No closures created in loops. No O(n^2) patterns: clipping is O(4) per line, drawLine is O(max(|deltaX|,|deltaY|)) per line, projection is O(n) over lines. No blocking I/O. No property access patterns that warrant local hoisting beyond what V8/JIT already does. Verdict: existing code is correct and the perf cost only applies once wired; deferring optimization until call-site wiring is the right call to avoid breaking the locked test hashes prematurely.

A candidate carrying `kind: 'user-local-iwad'` with `redistributesBytes: true` is semantically identical to redistributing proprietary IWAD bytes (the user simply being the redistributor), but the prior set silently classified it as `'redistributable-product-code'` and never raised. Default LOCAL_DISTRIBUTION_ASSET_CANDIDATES carries user-local-iwad with `redistributesBytes: false`, so default behavior was unaffected, but any malformed or malicious candidate (e.g., a future bundle artifact mislabelled as `user-local-iwad`) bypassed the policy guard. The MainLoop pre-loop sequence is run via `loop.setup()` only when `!loop.started`, recording `['initialTryRunTics','restoreBuffer','executeSetViewSize','startGameLoop']` matching `PRE_LOOP_STEPS`. The per-frame `runOneFrame()` records `['startFrame','tryRunTics','updateSounds','display']` matching `MAIN_LOOP_PHASES`. In `tryRunTics`, the toggle logic is correct: if `togglePauseMenu` (default true), `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` is flipped; if the resulting `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` is true, the callback returns early without calling `advanceLauncherSession` (gameplay does not advance, levelTime stays); otherwise `advanceLauncherSession(session, gameplayInput)` runs and `gameplayAdvanced` is set to true. The four truth-table branches (toggle×prior-state) all reach the correct gameplay-advance/no-advance outcome. `EMPTY_LAUNCHER_INPUT` is the documented frozen default; the test spreads it with overrides which is correct frozen-object usage. Defensive throw `'pause menu overlay flow did not complete a full main-loop frame'` guards against any callback path that fails to set `displayedFramebuffer`, `renderPhase`, or `tickPhase`. The result is `Object.freeze`-locked with `phaseTrace`/`preLoopTrace` spread into new arrays then frozen so external mutation is prevented. Cross-checked plan_fps/manifests/01-009-audit-missing-menu-to-e1m1.json: schemaVersion=1, stepId='01-009', commandContracts.targetRuntime.command='bun run doom.ts', explicitNullSurfaces contains `'menu-controller-surface'` and `'menu-render-surface'` with expectedPath:null — manifest schema and command contract are both locked by the focused test via toEqual/objectContaining/arrayContaining. The `as const` literal narrowing on the contract object is intentional to give `typeof WIRE_PAUSE_MENU_OVERLAY_FLOW_COMMAND_CONTRACT.command` the literal type `'bun run doom.ts'` rather than `string` (which makes the asserts-narrowing in `validateRuntimeCommand`'s signature precise). Edge cases verified: (1) options omitted → defaults `togglePauseMenu=true`, `pauseMenuOverlayOpen=false`, `command='bun run doom.ts'`, `gameplayInput=EMPTY_LAUNCHER_INPUT`, fresh `loop=new MainLoop()`; (2) `loop.started===true` already → setup skipped, `preLoopTrace=[]`; (3) callback throw path leaves `runOneFrame` mid-execution and skips the result-freeze; (4) `pauseMenuOverlayRenderedDuringDisplay` matches the value of `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` after `tryRunTics` because no later phase modifies it before `display` runs — but the capture site was at end-of-frame rather than during display, see improvement findings.
- performance_findings: none — function is invoked at most once per pause toggle event (boundary, not per-frame, per-tic, or per-pixel). - improvement_findings: (1) `pauseMenuOverlayRenderedDuringDisplay` was captured at the end of the frame (line 121 of the original file) by reading `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` post-runOneFrame. The captured value was correct only by accident: `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` is set in `tryRunTics` (which runs before `display` in the canonical phase order) and not modified afterward. If a future maintainer added a phase callback that toggled `pauseMenuOverlayOpen` after `display` (or moved the toggle), the captured value would silently drift from the true display-time value. (2) Test coverage gap: the four (togglePauseMenu × pauseMenuOverlayOpen) branches were only tested for togglePauseMenu=true (both starting states); the togglePauseMenu=false branches (legitimate "render-without-toggling" use-cases — render a frame in normal play with no toggle, or render a frame while paused with no toggle) had zero test coverage.

Display-time semantics are now explicit and robust against future phase-callback reordering. (2) Added two regression tests covering the previously-untested togglePauseMenu=false branches: `'advances gameplay deterministically when togglePauseMenu is false and the overlay is closed'` (asserts gameplayAdvanced=true, levelTimeAfter=1, pauseMenuOverlayOpenAfter=false, pauseMenuOverlayRenderedDuringDisplay=false, full phaseTrace) and `'keeps gameplay paused when togglePauseMenu is false and the overlay is already open'` (asserts gameplayAdvanced=false, levelTimeAfter=0, pauseMenuOverlayOpenAfter=true, pauseMenuOverlayRenderedDuringDisplay=true, full phaseTrace). (3) Updated the locked formatted-source SHA-256 from `1f520de106bf21ee85e916766fe0aff9a856166012ec5ba49e2047463afbabe1` to `1afb9902348625ec8efb790c60966b12112b18ceea6eaf8631404d0f3a4f9967` to match the formatted source after the capture-site move. Test count grew from 6 (33 expects) to 8 (47 expects). No command contract changes, no manifest edits, no plan-file edits beyond AUDIT_LOG.md.

Per-window validation order: validateNonNegativeInteger(firstGameTic) → validateNonNegativeInteger(lastGameTic) → throw RangeError when lastGameTic<firstGameTic → per-event captureEventSignature which validates event.gameTic in [firstGameTic, lastGameTic]. Music actions validated per kind: pause-song/resume-song no extra checks; play-song validates musicNum in [1,67] then scoreHash via /^[a-f0-9]{64}$/ (lowercase hex 64 chars, null rejected); set-volume validates volume in [0,127]; stop-song validates musicNum in [1,67]. These ranges match musicSystem.ts constants verbatim — MUS_NONE=0/NUMMUSIC=68 → (0,68) inclusive ⇒ [1,67]; MUSIC_VOLUME_MIN=0/MUSIC_VOLUME_MAX=127. Sound-effect results: inaudible/link-silenced/no-channel signed as their kind only; started validates cnum, pitch, separation, sfxId, volume all as non-negative integers. The captured event signature shape is `tic={n}:music:...` or `tic={n}:sound-effect:...` joined by ';' inside `window:{first}-{last}:...` and aggregate `audio-hash-window-schema=1|{windowHash1}|{windowHash2}|...`. SHA-256 hashing via Bun.CryptoHasher is bit-deterministic. checksumFromHash takes the first 8 hex chars and parseInts as base-16 (uint32). Output Object.freeze applied to result, result.windows array, and each capturedWindow object. Cross-checked src/audio/musicSystem.ts: every MusicDeviceAction variant (pause-song/play-song/resume-song/set-volume/stop-song) is handled in musicActionSignature; every StartSoundResult variant (inaudible/link-silenced/no-channel/started) is handled in soundEffectResultSignature. No correctness defect found in source.
- performance_findings: none — function is invoked once per replay capture window batch (boundary, not per-frame, per-tic, per-pixel, or per-sample). Per-window allocations: one event-signature array via window.events.map (bounded by event count), one windowSignature string concat, one Object.freeze of the captured window object. Aggregate allocations: capturedWindows array, capturedWindows.map for the join over windowHashes, captureSignature string, two SHA-256 hash digests (one per window plus one aggregate). Identified four test-coverage gaps inside the audited step's original scope: (1) the contract's currentPackageStartScript='bun run src/main.ts' was not cross-checked against the live package.json, so a drift in package.json's scripts.start would silently invalidate the transition record; (2) requiredLocalFiles entries had no uniqueness invariant on path or category, so a duplicate documentation entry would silently pass deep-equal until someone explicitly read the array; (3) the documentationHash was locked only by an opaque hex string, so the implementation could in principle have desynced from its declared inputs (rename a field while keeping the hash stale, etc.) and the test would still pass; (4) no granular lock confirms the hash function's domain — recomputing it inside the test from the public contract surface verifies the implementation's hash is computed exactly over (commandContract, deterministicReplayCompatibility, requiredLocalFiles, transition) in that key order.
- performance_findings: none — documentRequiredLocalFiles is a startup-time documentation surface (not per-frame/per-tic/per-sample/per-pixel/per-lump). The SHA-256 over the small frozen contract JSON is computed once at module load via Bun.CryptoHasher and cached on DOCUMENT_REQUIRED_LOCAL_FILES_EVIDENCE; subsequent calls return the same frozen reference. requiredLocalFiles is a 4-entry frozen tuple so Object.freeze and JSON.stringify costs are negligible.
- improvement_findings: Three drift-detector gaps inside scope. (1) The transition record claims 'bun run src/main.ts' is the current package start script but the live package.json was never asserted to match. (2) requiredLocalFiles uniqueness on path and category was unanchored. (3) The documentationHash was an opaque lock — the test should also recompute the hash from the public inputs and assert equality so future changes that update one without the other are caught.
- corrective_action: Added three regression tests inside the existing describe block in test/playable/bun-launch-local-distribution-boundary/document-required-local-files.test.ts. (a) 'aligns the documented current package start script with the live package.json' loads the live package.json via Bun.file(new URL('../../../package.json', import.meta.url)).json() and asserts pkg.scripts.start equals both the literal 'bun run src/main.ts' and DOCUMENT_REQUIRED_LOCAL_FILES_TRANSITION.currentPackageStartScript — locking the cross-field invariant. (b) 'keeps every required local file path and category unique' walks DOCUMENT_REQUIRED_LOCAL_FILES_REQUIRED_FILES and asserts no path or category repeats, plus that the resulting Set sizes match the array length, defending against silent duplicate-entry drift. (c) 'reproduces the documentation hash from the public contract inputs' calls documentRequiredLocalFiles() and recomputes new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(JSON.stringify({commandContract, deterministicReplayCompatibility, requiredLocalFiles, transition})).digest('hex'), asserting it equals both evidence.documentationHash and the locked EXPECTED_DOCUMENTATION_HASH — locking the implementation's hash domain. Test count grew from 4 (24 expects) to 7 (38 expects). No production-source change to documentRequiredLocalFiles.ts — the contract already satisfies the new invariants.
